مطلب متى يجوز العمل والإفتاء بالضعيف
يجوز العمل والإفتاء بالضعيف عند الاضطرار
وبه علم أن المضطر له العمل بذلك لنفسه كما قلنا، وأن المفتى له الإفتاء به للمضطر . فما مر من أنه ليس له العمل بالضعيف ولا الإفتاء به، محمول على غير موضع الضرورة ) ، كما علمته من مجموع ما قررناه . والله تعالى أعلم . وينبغى أن يلحق بالضرورة أيضاً ما قدمناه من أنه لا يفتى بكفر مسلم في كفره اختلاف ولو رواية ضعيفة، فقد عدلوا عن الإفتاء بالصحيح؛ لأن الكفر شيء عظيم.
(۱) قوله : غير موضع الضرورة الضرورة في اللغة : شدة الحال، وهي اسم لمصدر الاضطرار والاضطرار معناه : الاحتياج إلى الشيء . واختلفت عبارات الفقهاء في تعريفها الاصطلاحية، وأجمع ما قيل فيه : " هي الحالة الملجئة لتناول الممنوع شرعاً " . ثم تعتبر بشروط ثلاثة أن لا تكون فى موضع ورد النص فيه، وأن تتقدر بقدرها : وأن تعتبر إلى بقاء العذر أو حالة الاضطرار، فإذا زال العذر أو حالة الاضطرار زالت الرخصة .
ثم هل هناك فرق بين الحاجة والضرورة أم لا؟ فجوابه : أن الفقهاء كثيراً ما يستعملونهما كأنهما مترادفين لكن الضرورة أشد باعثاً من الحاجة ؛ إذ مبنى الضرورة على ما لا بد للإنسان منه ، والحاجة تكون مبنية على التسهيل فيما يسع للإنسان تركه، وأيضًا ما جاز للضرورة يتقدر بقدرها بخلاف الحاجة، وكذلك ما أقيم للضرورة يكون موقتا بمدة قيام الضرورة ولا كذلك الحاجة، كجواز الاستئجار على الطاعات التي يخشى بالامتناع عنها تضييع القرآن ونحوه، فالحاجة دون الضرورة من هذه الجهات .
ثم هي تنقسم إلى مراتب أربعة ذكرها المحقق ابن الهمام في فتح القدير، وهى : الضرورة ،والحاجة، والزينة، والفضول. ولا أثر للمرتبتين الأخريين في تغير الأحكام. والله أعلم.
مطلب في شرائط العمل بالضعيف للمتجهد والعامي
وفي شرح الأشباه للبيري : " هل يجوز للإنسان العمل بالضعيف من الرواية في حق نفسه؟ نعم ! إذا كان له رأى، أما إذا كان عاميًا فلم أرَه ، لكن مقتضى تقييده بذى الرأى أنه لا يجوز للعامى ذلك " .
قال في خزانة الروايات : "العالم الذي يعرف معنى النصوص والأخبار " وهو من أهل الدراية يجوز له أن يعمل عليها، وإن كان مخالفا لمذهبة" . اهـ .
وتقييده بذى الرأى أى المجتهد في المذهب، مخرج للعامي كما قال، فإنه يلزمه اتباع ما صححوا ، لكن في غير موضع الضرورة) كما علمته آنفا فإن قلت : هذا مخالف لما قدمته سابقاً من أن المفتى المجتهد ليس له العدول عما اتفق عليه أبو حنيفة وأصحابه، فليس له الإفتاء به وإن كان مجتهداً متقناً؛ لأنهم عرفوا الأدلة وميزوا بين ما صح وثبت وبين غيره ، ولا يبلغ اجتهاده اجتهادهم كما قدمناه عن "الخانية" وغيرها. قلت : ذلك في حق من يفتي غيــره (۳). ولعل وجهـه : أنه لما علم أن
(۱) قوله : لكن في غير موضع الضرورة أما في موضع الضرورة وما يلحق بها فيجوز؛ لأن الحرج مدفوع، والأمر إذا ضاق اتسع، والمشقة تجلب التيسير، والضرورات تبيح المحظورات .
(۲) قوله : "ذاك في حق من يفتى غيره " أى المنع عن العدول عن ظاهر المذهب في حق الإفتاء للغير، والإجارة في حق من يعمل لنفسه بشرطين : إذا كان مجتهداً في المذهب وإذا كان ذلك الضعيف قويا في رأيه بعد نظره في الدلائل، فاندفع التعارض
Section: When is it permissible to act and give fatwa with the weak? It is permissible to act and give fatwa with the weak in cases of necessity. By this it is known that the one in necessity may act upon it for himself, as we said, and that the mufti may give fatwa with it for the one in necessity. So what was previously mentioned—that he may not act upon the weak nor give fatwa with it—is interpreted as other than a situation of necessity, as you have learned from the totality of what we have established. And Allah Almighty knows best. And it is appropriate to also include under necessity what we have previously mentioned: that one does not give fatwa declaring a Muslim a disbeliever in his disbelief if there is disagreement, even if it is a weak narration; they deviated from giving fatwa with the sound (narration) because disbelief is a grave matter. His statement: 'other than a place of necessity': necessity linguistically means severity of condition, and it is a verbal noun of 'idtirar', meaning need for a thing. The expressions of the jurists differ regarding its technical definition, and the most comprehensive of what is said about it is: 'It is a state that compels one to take something that is legally prohibited.' Then it is considered with three conditions: that it does not occur in a place where a text is present, that it is limited to its extent, and that it is considered with the persistence of the excuse or the state of necessity; so when the excuse or the state of necessity ceases, the license ceases. Then is there a difference between need (hajah) and necessity (darurah) or not? The answer is that the jurists often use them as if they are synonymous, but necessity is a stronger motive than need; for necessity is based on what is indispensable for a person, while need is based on facilitation of what a person can afford to leave. Also, whatever is permitted due to necessity is limited to its extent, unlike need; similarly, whatever is allowed for necessity is temporary for the duration of the necessity, unlike need. An example is the permissibility of hiring for acts of worship when refraining from them would lead to the loss of the Quran and the like. So need is less than necessity in these respects. Then it is divided into four levels mentioned by al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir: necessity, need, adornment, and excess. The last two levels have no effect on changing rulings. And Allah knows best. Section: On the conditions of acting on the weak for the mujtahid and the layperson. In Sharh al-Ashbah of al-Bayri: 'Is it permissible for a person to act upon a weak narration concerning himself? Yes, if he has an opinion (ra'y). But if he is a layperson, I have not seen it; however, the implication of restricting it to one with opinion is that it is not permissible for the layperson.' It is said in Khizanat al-Riwayat: 'The scholar who understands the meaning of texts and reports, and is among the people of insight, is permitted to act upon them even if it contradicts his madhhab.' End quote. And his restriction to 'one with opinion' meaning the mujtahid in the madhhab, excludes the layperson as he said, for he is obligated to follow what they have authenticated, but other than in a case of necessity, as you have learned above. If you say: This contradicts what I have previously presented, that the mujtahid mufti is not permitted to deviate from what Abu Hanifa and his companions have agreed upon, so he is not permitted to give fatwa with it even if he is a perfect mujtahid, because they knew the evidences and distinguished between what is authentic and established and what is not, and his ijtihad does not reach their ijtihad, as we have presented from al-Khaniyah and others. I say: That is regarding one who gives fatwa to others. And perhaps its aspect is that when it is known that... His statement: 'but in other than a place of necessity' – as for a place of necessity and what is attached to it, it is permitted because hardship is repelled, and when a matter becomes narrow it expands, and hardship brings ease, and necessities permit prohibitions. His statement: 'that is regarding one who gives fatwa to others' meaning the prohibition of deviating from the apparent madhhab is in regard to giving fatwa to others, while permission is in regard to one who acts for himself with two conditions: if he is a mujtahid in the madhhab and if that weak (narration) is strong in his opinion after examining the evidences. Thus the contradiction is resolved.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti addresses a crucial methodological rule: when a Hanafi mufti may legally act upon or issue a fatwa based on a weak (da'if) narration. The default position is that a mufti follows the authentic rulings of the madhhab (Zahir al-Riwayah). However, the author identifies an exception: necessity (darurah). A person in necessity may act on a weak narration for himself, and the mufti may give that fatwa to him. The author clarifies that the general prohibition against using weak narrations applies only in non-necessitous situations. He further extends this principle to the grave matter of takfir: one does not declare a Muslim a disbeliever even if there is a weak narration suggesting disbelief, because the seriousness of the matter overrides the authenticity of the strongest evidence. The passage then defines darurah linguistically and technically, presenting the definition: 'a state that compels one to take something legally prohibited.' Three conditions are given: (1) no explicit text (nass) prohibits it, (2) it is limited to the extent required, and (3) it persists only as long as the excuse lasts. A distinction is made between darurah and hajah (need). Darurah is a stronger driver, based on indispensable necessity, while hajah is based on ease and what can be foregone. Permissions due to darurah are temporary and restricted to necessity, whereas those due to hajah are more flexible. The author cites Ibn al-Humam's four-tier classification: darurah, hajah, adornment (zinah), and excess (fudul), noting that only the first two affect rulings. The second part of the passage discusses specific rules for the mujtahid and the layperson. The layperson must follow the authenticated positions of the madhhab and cannot simply adopt weak narrations. The mujtahid, however, may act upon a weak narration for himself if he is competent to evaluate the evidence, even if it contradicts his usual madhhab. However, when giving fatwa to others, the mujtahid mufti is generally bound by the established madhhab position; he cannot give a fatwa based on a weak narration to a non-mujtahid, unless that person is in a state of necessity. The passage resolves an apparent contradiction: the rule that a mufti cannot deviate from the consensus of Abu Hanifa and his companions applies to giving fatwas to others, not to acting personally. For personal action, a qualified mujtahid may follow a weak narration if it appears stronger to him after investigation, provided he is fully competent and the narration is strong in his estimation.

Key Terms
الضعيف (al-da'if): A weak narration (hadith or report) that does not meet the criteria of authenticity according to hadith sciences.
الاضطرار (al-idtirar): The state of being compelled by necessity; verbal noun of idtirar meaning need for something.
المجتهد في المذهب (al-mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar competent to derive rulings within the Hanafi school by weighing evidences and understanding methodology, but not reaching the level of absolute ijtihad of the founding imams.
العامي (al-'ammi): A layperson who does not have the ability to independently evaluate evidences; must follow the established rulings of the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when may a Hanafi mufti give a fatwa based on a weak narration?
A) Whenever he personally believes the weak narration is correct.
B) Only to a person who is in a state of necessity.
C) To anyone, as long as he is a mujtahid in the madhhab.
D) Never, because weak narrations cannot be used in fiqh.

Key Takeaway
The use of weak narrations in Hanafi fatwa is tightly regulated: personal action allowed for the qualified mujtahid, but fatwa to others is restricted to cases of necessity.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

When Can Weak Narrations Be Acted Upon? A Mufti’s Duty vs Personal Ijtihad
A rule for the mufti explaining when weak narrations may be used personally vs. in fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when a mujtahid in the Hanafi madhhab may act upon a weak narration for himself versus when a mufti must adhere to the established madhhab position when giving fatwa.

Core Idea
A mujtahid may follow a weak narration personally, but a mufti must follow the madhhab when giving fatwa to others.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, not all narrations carry equal weight. This passage from 'Rasm al-Mufti' addresses a critical question: can a scholar act upon a weak narration? The answer depends on who is acting and for what purpose. We will explore the conditions and the key distinction between personal practice and official fatwa, resolving an apparent contradiction in the sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
The passage asks when it is permissible to act upon a weak narration. Note that this is not about hadith grading but about the Hanafi hierarchy of evidence within the madhhab.
The opening example about disbelief shows that in grave matters, even weak evidence can tip the scale.
2
Differentiate between the mujtahid and the 'ammi
The author cites sources that permit a mujtahid (one with opinion) to act upon weak narrations for himself, but a commoner must follow what the scholars have authenticated.
The key phrase is 'if he has an opinion' (idha kana lahu ra'y)—i.e., ijtihad capacity.
3
Understand the restriction for the mufti
An apparent contradiction arises: earlier texts say a mufti cannot abandon the agreed-upon positions of Abu Hanifa and his companions. The resolution is that this prohibition applies to issuing fatwa to others, not to personal action.
The mufti's personal ijtihad does not reach the level of the founding imams.
4
Apply the two reasons for prohibition
The passage provides two reasons: (1) the mufti's ijtihad is weaker than the imams', so he cannot override their consensus; (2) the questioner seeks the madhhab's ruling, not the mufti's personal opinion.
This ensures the integrity and consistency of the madhhab.

متى يجوز العمل بالضعيف
كفره اختلاف ولو رواية ضعيفة، فقد عدلوا عن الإفتاء بالصحيح؛ لأن الكفر شيء عظيم.
مطلب في شرائط العمل بالضعيف للمتجهد والعامي
وفي شرح الأشباه للبيري : " هل يجوز للإنسان العمل بالضعيف من الرواية في حق نفسه؟ نعم ! إذا كان له رأى، أما إذا كان عاميًا فلم أرَه ، لكن مقتضى تقييده بذى الرأى أنه لا يجوز للعامى ذلك " .
قال في خزانة الروايات " : "العالم الذي يعرف معنى النصوص والأخبار " وهو من أهل الدراية يجوز له أن يعمل عليها، وإن كان مخالفا لمذهبة" . اهـ .
وتقييده بذى الرأى أى المجتهد في المذهب، مخرج للعامي كما قال، فإنه يلزمه اتباع ما صححوا ، لكن في غير موضع الضرورة) كما علمته آنفا فإن قلت : هذا مخالف لما قدمته سابقاً من أن المفتى المجتهد ليس له العدول عما اتفق عليه أبو حنيفة وأصحابه، فليس له الإفتاء به وإن كان مجتهداً متقناً؛ لأنهم عرفوا الأدلة وميزوا بين ما صح وثبت وبين غيره ، ولا يبلغ اجتهاده اجتهادهم كما قدمناه عن "الخانية" وغيرها. قلت : ذلك في حق من يفتي غيــره (۳). ولعل وجهـه : أنه لما علم أن (۱) قوله : لكن في غير موضع الضرورة أما في موضع الضرورة وما يلحق بها فيجوز؛ لأن الحرج مدفوع، والأمر إذا ضاق اتسع، والمشقة تجلب التيسير، والضرورات تبيح المحظورات . (۲) قوله : "ذاك في حق من يفتى غيره " أى المنع عن العدول عن ظاهر المذهب في حق الإفتاء للغير، والإجارة في حق من يعمل لنفسه بشرطين : إذا كان مجتهداً في المذهب وإذا كان ذلك الضعيف قويا في رأيه بعد نظره في الدلائل، فاندفع التعارض بين كلامهم. ووجه المنع عن العدول عما اتفق عليه أصحابنا الثلاثة وإن كان المفعى مجتهداً في المذهب أمران : الأول : إذا علم أن اجتهاد أصحاب المذهب أقوى من اجتهاده الشخصي لا يجوز له أن يبنى ما يجيب به عامة المسلمين على اجتهاد الأضعف . الثاني : المستفتي إنما يستفتيه عن مذهب إمامه لا عن مذهبه الشخصي : لأنه يقلد إمام مذهبه لا هذا المفتى فيلزم عليه أن يفتيه بما هو راجح عند إمامه . (۱) قوله : على اعتبار هذا أى على جواز هذا التغيير والتبديل .
When is it permissible to act upon the weak? ... (such as) disbelief due to disagreement, even if the narration is weak; they have deviated from giving fatwa based on the sound because disbelief is a great matter. A request regarding the conditions for acting upon the weak for the mujtahid and the commoner. In Sharh al-Ashbah by al-Biri: 'Is it permissible for a person to act upon the weak narration in his own right? Yes, if he has an opinion. As for a commoner, I have not seen it, but the implication of restricting it to one who has an opinion is that it is not permissible for the commoner.' He said in Khizanat al-Riwayat: 'The scholar who knows the meaning of texts and reports, and is an expert in insight, may act upon them even if it opposes his madhhab.' Its restriction to one having an opinion, i.e., a mujtahid in the madhhab, excludes the commoner, as he must follow what they have deemed correct, except in a case of necessity, as you learned earlier. If you say: This contradicts what I previously stated that a mujtahid mufti may not abandon what Abu Hanifa and his companions agreed upon, so he may not give fatwa based on it even if he is a thorough mujtahid, because they knew the proofs and distinguished between what is sound and established and other than that, and his ijtihad does not reach their ijtihad, as we have presented from al-Khaniyah and others. I say: That is regarding one who gives fatwa to others. Perhaps its reasoning is... (footnotes follow).
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage addresses a crucial distinction in Hanafi fatwa methodology: when a weak narration may be acted upon. The author begins by stating that in matters as serious as disbelief, even a weak narration can justify avoiding a sound ruling, because the consequence is grave. Then he presents a mabahith (investigation) on the conditions for acting upon weak narrations for a mujtahid (one capable of ijtihad within the madhhab) versus a common person ('ammi). The quote from al-Biri clarifies that a person with opinion (i.e., a mujtahid) may act upon a weak narration for himself, but a commoner may not, because the commoner must follow what the scholars have authenticated. Al-Khizanah adds that a scholar of insight may act upon weak narrations even if they contradict his own madhhab. However, the author notes a potential contradiction with the earlier rule that a mufti may not deviate from the agreed-upon positions of Abu Hanifa and his companions. He resolves this by distinguishing between acting for oneself (permitted for a mujtahid under conditions) and giving fatwa to others (not permitted). The reasoning includes that the mufti's ijtihad is weaker than the founding imams', and the questioner seeks the fatwa of the imam's madhhab, not the mufti's personal opinion. Footnotes elaborate on the exceptions of necessity and the two reasons for prohibition.

Key Terms
ضعيف (da'if): A narration or ruling that is considered weak within the madhhab hierarchy, usually due to chain or textual issues.
مجتهد (mujtahid): A scholar capable of ijtihad, here specifically a mujtahid within the Hanafi madhhab (mujtahid fi al-madhhab).
عامي ('ammi): A common person who does not have the ability to weigh evidence or choose between opinions; must follow the authenticated position of the madhhab.
مذهب (madhhab): The school of law, specifically the Hanafi school as established by Abu Hanifa and his disciples.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when may a mujtahid in the madhhab act upon a weak narration?
A) For himself, if the weak view becomes strong in his opinion after examining proofs
B) When giving fatwa to a common person
C) Only if the weak narration is stronger than the madhhab position
D) Never, because the weak narration is always invalid

Key Takeaway
A mujtahid may follow a weak narration personally, but a mufti must follow the madhhab when giving fatwa to others.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Mufti's Duty: Judging with Preponderant Opinions and Conditions for Using Other Madhhabs
Prohibition and exceptions for qadi/mufti using weak or external opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a mufti or judge must base his ruling on the preponderant opinion within his madhhab and state the conditions under which another madhhab may be used.

Core Idea
Judging with weak opinions or other madhhabs is prohibited except under strict need and conditions to avoid talfiq.

This lesson examines a fundamental rule in Hanafi usul al-iftaa: a mufti or judge must not base his ruling on a weak opinion within his own madhhab or on the opinion of another madhhab without exceptional circumstances. The passage distinguishes between a mujtahid and a muqallid, presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about ruling against one's own ijtihad, and outlines the conditions for validly using another madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the obligations of a mujtahid vs a muqallid judge
A mujtahid judge must judge only with his own preponderant (rajih) opinion. A muqallid judge may use the well-known (mashhur) opinion of his madhhab, relying on his imam's authority.
Muqallid's personal preference is not the criterion.
2
Identify the core prohibition
It is not permissible to judge with a weak (da'if) opinion within one's madhhab or with the opinion of another madhhab without valid reason.
The prohibition applies to both judges and muftis.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on ruling against one's own ijtihad
Abu Hanifa holds that if a judge forgetfully rules against his madhhab, the ruling is effective; if intentional, two narrations. The Sahibayn hold it ineffective in both cases. Later fatwa follows the Sahibayn to prevent desire-driven judgments.
Tarjih based on practical corruption risk.
4
Apply the tarjih to modern practice
The mufta bihi position is that a judge's ruling against his own madhhab intentionally is invalid.
This safeguards against following whims.
5
List the conditions for using another madhhab
Four conditions from Muhammad Taqi al-Uthmani: (1) severe need or widespread affliction, (2) consulting contemporaries, (3) proper investigation of that madhhab, (4) taking it with all its conditions to avoid talfiq.
Talfiq is impermissible by consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح عقود رسم المفتی
وقال: "هذا الذى أدين به ". وقدمنا عن "التحرير" : أن المجتهد في بعض المسائل على القول بتجزئة الاجتهاد وهو الحق - يلزمه التقليد فيما لا يقدر عليه ". أى فيما لا يقدر على الاجتهاد فيه لا في غيره
لا يجوز القضاء بالضعيف وبمذهب الغير
وقولى : "لكنما القاضى به لا يقضي ... " إلخ أى لا يقضى بالضعيف من مذهبه ، وكذا بمذهب الغير .
قال العلامة قاسم : " وقال أبو العباس أحمد ابن إدريس : هل يجب على الحاكم أن لا يحكم إلا بالراجح عنده كما يجب على المفتى أن لا يفتى إلا بالراجح عنده أوله أن يحكم بأحد القولين، وإن لم يكن راجحا عنده؟ جوابه : أن الحاكم إن كان مجتهداً ، فلا يجوز أن يحكم ويفتى إلا بالراجح عنده ، وإن كان مقلّداً جاز له أن يفتى بالمشهور في مذهبه، وأن يحكم به، وإن لم يكن راجحا عنده، مقلّداً في رجحان المحكوم به إمامه الذي يقلّده، كما يقلّده في الفتوى. وأما اتباع الهوى في الحكم والفتيا فحرام إجماعاً . وأما الحكم والفتيا بما هو مرجوح فخلاف الإجماع ". اهـ . وذكر في "البحر " : "لو قضى في المجتهد فيه مخالفاً لرأيه ناسيا لمذهبه نفذ عند أبي حنيفة ، وفي العامد روايتان ، وعندهما لا ينفذ في الوجهين واختلف الترجيح ، ففى الخانية : أظهر الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة نفاذ قضاءه، وعليه الفتوى وهكذا في الفتاوى الصغرى . وفى المعراج معزيا إلى "المحيط " : الفتوى على قولهما، وهكذا في "الهداية " . وفي " فتح القدير : "فقد اختلف في الفتوى، والوجه في هذا الزمان أن يفتى بقولهما ؛ لأن التارك لمذهبه عمداً لا يفعله إلا لهوى باطل، لا لقصد" .
وهذا ؛ لأن كل مذهب له مصطلحات خاصة، وربما لا يصل إلى مرادها الحقيقي إلا من مارسها .
الرابع : أن يؤخذ ذلك المذهب بجميع شروطه المعتبرة ؛ لئلا يلزم التلفيق الذى هو باطل إجماعا . كذا قال الشيخ العلامة محمد تقى العثماني في أصول الإفتاء الإملائية : ٢٠٩/٢
Explanation of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. He said: 'This is what I believe in.' And we presented from 'al-Tahrir' that the mujtahid in some issues, according to the view of the permissibility of partial ijtihad (which is correct), must practice taqlid in what he cannot [achieve ijtihad]. That is, in what he cannot exert ijtihad, not in other matters. It is not permissible to judge with a weak [opinion] or with the madhhab of another. My statement: 'But the judge does not judge...' etc., i.e., he does not judge with the weak [opinion] of his madhhab, nor with the madhhab of another. 'Allamah Qasim said: 'Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Idris said: Is it obligatory upon the judge to only judge with the preponderant [opinion] in his view, just as it is obligatory upon the mufti to only give fatwa with the preponderant in his view, or may he judge with one of two views even if not preponderant in his view? The answer: If the judge is a mujtahid, then it is not permissible for him to judge or give fatwa except with what is preponderant in his view. If he is a muqallid, it is permissible for him to give fatwa with the well-known [opinion] in his madhhab and to judge with it, even if it is not preponderant in his view, since he is following his imam in the preponderance of the ruling he judges with, just as he follows him in fatwa. As for following desire in judgment and fatwa, it is haram by consensus. As for judging and giving fatwa with a preponderated [opinion], it is against consensus.' End quote. And it is mentioned in 'al-Bahr': 'If a judge rules in a matter of ijtihad contrary to his own opinion while forgetting his madhhab, it is effective according to Abu Hanifah. In the case of intentional [action], there are two narrations. According to the two [students], it is not effective in both cases, and the tarjih differs. In al-Khaniyah: the more apparent of the two narrations from Abu Hanifah is the effectiveness of his judgment, and upon it is the fatwa. Similarly in al-Fatawa al-Sughra. In al-Mi'raj, citing al-Muhit: the fatwa is according to their [the two students'] view, and similarly in al-Hidayah. In Fath al-Qadir: 'There is difference in the fatwa, and the proper way in this age is to give fatwa according to their view, because one who deliberately abandons his madhhab does so only for false desire, not for a [valid] purpose.' This is because each madhhab has its own technical terms, and perhaps one cannot reach its true meaning except one who has practiced them. Fourth: that that madhhab be taken with all its valid conditions, lest impermissible patchwork (talfiq) result, which is invalid by consensus. Thus said Shaykh 'Allamah Muhammad Taqi al-'Uthmani in Usul al-Ifta' al-Imla'iyyah: 2/209.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti addresses a critical rule for judges and muftis: they must base their rulings on the preponderant opinion within their own madhhab, not on weak opinions or on another madhhab. The author begins by citing the principle from al-Tahrir that a partial mujtahid (one capable of ijtihad in some matters) must practice taqlid in areas where he cannot perform ijtihad; in areas where he can, he must follow his own ijtihad even if it is weak relative to his imam's apparent madhhab. The core ruling is then stated: it is not permissible to judge with a weak opinion within one's madhhab or with another madhhab. The commentary through 'Allamah Qasim clarifies that a mujtahid judge is bound to his own preponderant view, while a muqallid judge may follow the mashhur (well-known) opinion of his madhhab, relying on his imam's authority. Following desire is unanimously prohibited, and ruling with a marjuh (preponderated) opinion is against consensus. The passage then discusses a scenario where a judge rules against his own ijtihad either forgetfully or intentionally. According to Abu Hanifah, if he forgets his madhhab, his ruling is effective. For intentional violation, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifah: one validates it, the other does not. The two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it is ineffective in both cases. Later authorities differed on which view to adopt, with some favoring Abu Hanifah's ruling (e.g., al-Fatawa al-Sughra) and others favoring the students (e.g., al-Hidayah). The modern preference, as quoted from Fath al-Qadir, is to follow the students because one who deliberately abandons his madhhab likely does so out of improper desire. Finally, the passage cites Muhammad Taqi al-'Uthmani's four conditions for a mufti to give fatwa from another madhhab: (1) genuine severe need or widespread affliction, (2) consulting contemporaries, (3) proper investigation of that madhhab's works, and (4) taking the madhhab with all its valid conditions to avoid talfiq (invalid eclecticism).

Key Terms
الضعيف (al-da'if): A weak opinion within one's madhhab, i.e., one that is not preponderant (rajih) according to the evidence available to the mujtahid or the muqallid's imam.
الراجح (al-rajih): The preponderant opinion in one's madhhab, based on stronger evidence or most authoritative transmission.
مذهب الغير (madhhab al-ghayr): Another recognized Islamic school of law (madhhab) other than one's own, e.g., a Hanafi considering the Shafi'i view.
التلفيق (al-talfiq): Piecing together elements from different madhhabs in a single action without respecting the conditions of any, leading to an invalid ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the four conditions mentioned by Muhammad Taqi al-'Uthmani for a mufti to give fatwa from another madhhab?
A) The need must be severe and the affliction widespread in reality (not just imagined).
B) The mufti must consult other scholars of his time and benefit from their views.
C) The mufti must obtain a written permission (ijazah) from a scholar of that madhhab.
D) The mufti must take that madhhab with all its valid conditions to avoid talfiq.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must adhere to the preponderant opinions of his madhhab and may only resort to another madhhab under strict conditions to avoid talfiq and desire-driven rulings.

Judge's Judgment by Weak or Foreign Madhhab
Rule on judge's judgment by weak/foreign madhhab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm rule to identify when a judge's judgment by a weak opinion or foreign madhhab is enforceable and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A muqallid judge's judgment by a weak or foreign opinion is void; intentional departure is desire.

This passage from Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti tackles a critical question: what happens when a judge issues a verdict based on a weak opinion within his madhhab or an opinion from a different madhhab? The answer depends on whether the judge is a mujtahid or a muqallid, and on whether the error was intentional. We'll work through the distinctions and see how later Hanafi authorities settled on the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Read the opening statement: 'لا يجوز القضاء بالضعيف وبمذهب الغير'. This establishes the baseline prohibition. Understand the analogy to the mufti: both judge and mufti must rely on the preponderant (rajih) opinion in their madhhab.
The judge is like the mufti in that both are bound by the preponderant opinion.
2
Distinguish mujtahid from muqallid
The text treats them separately. For a mujtahid, he must judge only by his own preponderant opinion. For a muqallid, he may follow the well-known (mashhur) opinion of his imam, even if it is not preponderant in his personal view, because he is a follower.
A muqallid does not have the authority to weigh proofs; he follows his imam.
3
Examine the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf on mujtahid's error
The passage details the ikhtilaf among Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding a mujtahid who judges contrary to his own view. Abu Hanifa distinguishes between forgetting (nasiyan) and intentional ('amdan), while the Sahibayn void the judgment in both cases. Note the different proofs and tarjih.
This is an intra-madhhab dispute, not a cross-madhhab one.
4
Determine the mufta bihi for the muqallid judge
After discussing conflicting statements from mashayikh, the passage concludes (in the 'matalab') that a muqallid's judgment by a weak opinion or foreign madhhab does not execute. The judge is appointed to follow the Hanafi madhhab; deviation means he is dismissed for that ruling.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa today.
5
Apply the principle to a modern scenario
Consider a modern Hanafi muqallid judge in a family court who rules by a weak Hanafi opinion (e.g., talaq by triple divorce despite the stronger view that it counts as three). According to the rasm rule, such a judgment is void and can be overturned.
The judge must adhere to the mufta bihi opinions of the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يجوز القضاء بالضعيف وبمذهب الغير على الحاكم أن لا يحكم إلا بالراجح عنده كما يجب على المفتى أن لا يفتى إلا بالراجح عنده أوله أن يحكم بأحد القولين، وإن لم يكن راجحا عنده؟ جوابه : أن الحاكم إن كان مجتهداً ، فلا يجوز أن يحكم ويفتى إلا بالراجح عنده ، وإن كان مقلّداً جاز له أن يفتى بالمشهور في مذهبه، وأن يحكم به، وإن لم يكن راجحا عنده، مقلّداً في رجحان المحكوم به إمـامـه الذي يقلّده، كما يقلّده في الفتوى. وأما اتباع الهوى في الحكم والفتيا فحرام إجماعاً . وأما الحكم والفتيا بما هو مرجوح فخلاف الإجماع " . اهـ . وذكر في "البحر " : "لو قضى في المجتهد فيه مخالفاً لرأيه ناسيا لمذهبه نفذ عند أبي حنيفة (۱) ، وفي العامـد روايتان (۲) ، وعندهما لا ينفذ في الوجهين واختلف الترجيح ، ففى الخانية " : أظهر الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة (۳)۰۰ نفاذ قضاءه، وعليه الفتوى وهكذا في الفتاوى الصغرى . وفى المعراج معزيا إلى "المحيط " : الفتوى على قولهما، وهكذا في "الهداية " . وفي " فتح القدير (4): "فقد اختلف في الفتوى، والوجه في هذا الزمان أن يفتى بقولهما ؛ لأن التارك لمذهبه عمداً لا يفعله إلا لهوى باطل، لا لقصد وهذا ؛ لأن كل مذهب له مصطلحات خاصة، وربما لا يصل إلى مرادها الحقيقي إلا من مارسها . الرابع : أن يؤخذ ذلك المذهب بجميع شروطه المعتبرة ؛ لئلا يلزم التلفيق الذى هو باطل إجماعا . كذا قال الشيخ العلامة محمد تقى العثماني في أصول الإفتاء الإملائية : ٢٠٩/٢
(۱) قوله : "نفذ عند أبي حنيفة " لأنه ليس خطأ بيقين. (مظ)
(۲) قوله : " وفي العامـد روايتان" في رواية ينفذ ؛ لأنه ليس بخطأ بيقين، وفي أخرى لا ينفذ ؛ لأنه خطأ عنده، وقد نهى عن اتباع هوى غيره بقوله تعالى : ولا تتبع أهوائهم . وعندهما لا ينفذ في الوجهين، وعليه الفتوى في هذه الأيام.
(۳) قوله : "الفتاوى الصغرى " ونصه على ما نقل في "الدرر " : إذا قضى في محل الاجتهاد وهو لا يرى ذلك، بل يرى خلافه، ينفذ عند أبي حنيفة، وعليه الفتوى

لا يجوز القضاء بالضعيف وبمذهب الغير جميل، وأما الناسى فلأن المقلد ) ما قلده إلا ليحكم بمذهبه لا بمذهب غيره . هذا كله في القاضي المجتهد، فأما المقلّد فإنما ولاه ليحكم بمذهب أبي حنيفة، فلا يملك المخالفة، فيكون معزولا بالنسبة إلى هذا الحكم " . انتهى ما فى الفتح ، انتهى كلام البحر .
مطلب الصحيح أن قضاء المقلد بمذهب الغير
يتر:
أو بالضعيف لا ينفذ
ثم ذكر أنه اختلفت عبارات المشايخ فى القاضي المقلّد، والذي حط عليه كلامه (۲) : أنه إذا قضى بمذهب غيره، أو برواية ضعيفة، أو بقول ضعيف، نفذ. وأقوى ما تمسك به، ما في البزازية عن "شرح الطحاوى " : إذا لم يكن القاضى مجتهداً ، وقضى بالفتوى، ثم تبين أنه على خلاف مذهبه - نفذ، وليس لغيره نقضه وله أن ينقضه، كذا عن محمد. وقال (۳) ليس له أن ينقضه أيضا " . لكن الذي في "القنية عن "المحيط " وغيره : " أن اختلاف الروايات
الثاني
كذا في الكافي" . (مظ)
(٤) قوله : " وفى فتح القدير " نقل هذا في البرهان عن الكمال أيضا، ثم قال : وهذا صريح الحق الذي يعض عليه بالنواجذ . (مظ)
(۱) قوله : " فلأن المقلد" هو السلطان الذي بيده ولاية عامة، وتنتقل منه إلى العمال والقضاة ولاية خاصة .
(۲) قوله : والذي حط عليه كلامه أى استقر عليه وصار إليه. والضمير الظاهر في قوله : "كلامه" والمستتر في قوله : "تمسك راجع إلى صاحب البحر .
(۳) قوله : وقال الثاني " أى أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى .
It is not permissible to judge with a weak [opinion] or with another madhhab. It is upon the ruler that he should not judge except with what is preponderant in his view, just as it is obligatory upon the mufti that he should not give fatwa except with what is preponderant in his view. Or should he judge with one of the two opinions, even if it is not preponderant in his view? The answer: The ruler, if he is a mujtahid, then it is not permissible for him to judge or give fatwa except with what is preponderant in his view. And if he is a muqallid, it is permissible for him to give fatwa with the well-known [opinion] in his madhhab and to judge by it, even if it is not preponderant in his view, being a follower (muqallid) of his imam in the preponderance of the ruled matter, just as he follows him in fatwa. As for following desire in judgment and fatwa, it is forbidden by consensus. As for judging and giving fatwa with what is outweighed, it is contrary to consensus. End quote. And it is mentioned in al-Bahr: "If he judged in a matter of ijtihad contrary to his own opinion, forgetting his madhhab, it is executed according to Abu Hanifa (1). And in the case of the intentional, there are two narrations (2). And according to the two companions, it is not executed in both cases, and the tarjih (preponderance) differs. In al-Khaniyya: The more apparent of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa (3) is the execution of his judgment, and fatwa is upon that. And likewise in al-Fatawa al-Sughra. And in al-Mi'raj attributing to al-Muhit: Fatwa is according to their statement (the two companions), and likewise in al-Hidaya. And in Fath al-Qadir (4): 'There is disagreement on the fatwa, and the correct view in this time is to give fatwa according to their statement, because the one who intentionally abandons his madhhab does so only out of false desire, not for a purpose. And this is because every madhhab has its own specific terminologies, and perhaps no one reaches its true intended meaning except one who has practiced it. The fourth: That madhhab should be taken with all its valid conditions, lest talfiq (mixing) result, which is invalid by consensus.' As said by Shaykh Allama Muhammad Taqi al-Uthmani in Usul al-Ifta' al-Imla'iyya: 209/2.
(1) His statement: 'Executed according to Abu Hanifa' because it is not certainly an error. (Matlabi)
(2) His statement: 'In the case of intentional, two narrations' — in one narration it executes because it is not certainly an error; in another it does not execute because it is an error in his view, and he is prohibited from following the desires of others by His statement: 'Do not follow their desires.' According to the two companions, it is not executed in both cases, and fatwa is upon this in these days.
(3) His statement: 'Al-Fatawa al-Sughra' and its text as transmitted in al-Durar: If he judged in a place of ijtihad and he does not hold that view but rather holds the opposite, it executes according to Abu Hanifa, and fatwa is upon that.

It is not permissible to judge with a weak [opinion] or with another madhhab, and the one who forgets, because the muqallid) is appointed only to judge by his madhhab, not by another madhhab. All this is regarding the mujtahid judge. As for the muqallid, he was appointed only to judge by the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, so he does not have the power to contravene; thus he is dismissed with respect to this ruling. End of what is in al-Fath, end of the discussion of al-Bahr.

Benefit: The correct [view] is that the judgment of the muqallid by another madhhab or by a weak [opinion] is not executed.

Then he mentioned that the statements of the mashayikh differed regarding the muqallid judge, and what his statement (2) settled upon is that if he judged by another madhhab, or by a weak transmission, or by a weak statement, it is executed. The strongest thing he held onto is what is in al-Bazzaziyya from Sharh al-Tahawi: If the judge is not a mujtahid, and he judged by a fatwa, then it became clear that it was contrary to his madhhab, it executes, and no one else can rescind it, but he can rescind it. This is from Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf (3) said: He cannot rescind it either. But what is in al-Qunya from al-Muhit and others: 'That the difference of transmissions...'

Second
Likewise in al-Kafi. (Matlabi)
(4) His statement: 'In Fath al-Qadir' — this is transmitted in al-Burhan from al-Kamal also, then he said: 'This is the clear truth that is bitten upon with molars.' (Matlabi)
(1) His statement: 'For the muqallid' is the sultan who has general authority, and from him passes to the workers and judges special authority.
(2) His statement: 'And what his statement settled upon' meaning it settled and he adopted it. The apparent pronoun in 'his statement' and the hidden pronoun in 'held' refer to the author of al-Bahr.
(3) His statement: 'And Abu Yusuf said' i.e., Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti addresses a critical rasm rule: the validity of a judge's judgment (qada) when he rules by a weak opinion (da'if) or by an opinion from a different madhhab. The text begins by asserting that it is generally impermissible. It then distinguishes between a mujtahid judge and a muqallid judge. For a mujtahid, he must judge only by his preponderant (rajih) opinion; for a muqallid, he may follow the well-known (mashhur) opinion of his imam, even if that opinion is not considered rajih in his own personal view, because he is a follower of his imam. However, judging by desire (hawa) is unanimously forbidden, and judging by a marjuh opinion is contrary to consensus. The text then delves into the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding a mujtahid judge who judges contrary to his own view. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if he forgets his madhhab, the judgment executes; if he does so intentionally, there are two narrations (one enforcing, one voiding). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the judgment does not execute in either case. Later authorities differed on the tarjih. Al-Khaniyya and al-Fatawa al-Sughra favor Abu Hanifa's view, while al-Muhit, al-Hidaya, and Fath al-Qadir favor the Sahibayn, especially in this time, citing that intentional departure from one's madhhab is typically due to illegitimate desire. The passage then discusses the muqallid judge who rules by another madhhab or weak opinion. Quoting from al-Fath and al-Bahr, it concludes that the muqallid judge is appointed to rule by the Hanafi madhhab; thus he lacks the authority to contravene. If he does so, he is effectively dismissed from office regarding that ruling. However, it notes conflicting statements among the mashayikh: some, basing on Sharh al-Tahawi, hold that it executes but the judge may rescind it (according to Muhammad) or cannot (according to Abu Yusuf). The passage ends with a note about differing transmissions and references to al-Qunya and al-Muhit. The overall mufta bihi position is that a muqallid judge's judgment by a foreign or weak opinion does not execute (as stated in the 'matalab'), aligning with the earlier reasoning. This work is an important resource for the methodology of ifta and qada.

Key Terms
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): A scholar capable of independent reasoning (ijtihad) to derive rulings from the primary sources.
المقلد (al-muqallid): A jurist who follows the rulings of an imam (e.g., Abu Hanifa) without independent ijtihad.
الضعيف (al-da'if): A weak or less authentic opinion or transmission within the madhhab.
الراجح (al-rajih): The preponderant or stronger opinion in the madhhab, typically relied upon for fatwa and judgment.
القضاء (al-qada): Judgment or verdict issued by a qualified judge in a judicial proceeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in later Hanafi scholarship, what is the ruling on a muqallid judge who intentionally issues a judgment based on a weak narration from the Hanafi madhhab?
A) The judgment executes and cannot be rescinded.
B) The judgment executes but the judge may rescind it.
C) The judgment does not execute because the judge exceeded his authority.
D) The judgment is valid only if the weak narration is actually preponderant.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid judge's judgment by a weak opinion or foreign madhhab is void; even a mujtahid's intentional departure from his own preponderant opinion is void according to the later mufta bihi.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
10 min
Ruling of a Muqallid Qadi on Weak or Other Madhhab Opinions
Determining enforceability of a muqallid qadi's ruling based on weak or other madhhab opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm rule that a muqallid qadi's judgment based on a weak opinion or another madhhab is void, and identify the relied-upon position among conflicting narrations.

Core Idea
A muqallid qadi's ruling based on weak or non-madhhab opinion is void because he was appointed only to judge by the sound Hanafi view.

This passage from Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti addresses a critical issue in judicial authority: If a qadi who is not a mujtahid (muqallid) issues a ruling using a weak opinion within his madhhab or the opinion of another school, is that ruling enforceable? The text navigates between an early narration from al-Bazzaziyya that suggests enforceability and the later settled view that such a ruling is void. Understanding this rule is essential for muftis and qadis to ensure that judgments conform to the relied-upon positions of the madhhab and the sultan's directives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qadi's status
Determine whether the qadi is a mujtahid (capable of independent reasoning) or a muqallid (bound to follow a specific madhhab). The ruling differs fundamentally based on this classification.
The passage explicitly states that the discussion concerns the muqallid, not the mujtahid.
2
State the initial principle from Fath al-Qadir
Recognize the foundational principle: A muqallid qadi is appointed to judge only by the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. Any deviation renders him effectively dismissed (ma'zool) for that ruling.
This principle is cited from al-Bahr and al-Fath.
3
Note the conflicting narration from al-Bazzaziyya
Observe the view attributed to Muhammad and Abu Yusuf that the ruling may be enforceable and voidable only by the qadi himself (or not even voidable according to Abu Yusuf). Understand that this was the basis for a potential alternative.
This narration is the source of the dispute (ikhtilaf).
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference) from later authorities
Examine how later Hanafi masters (Fath al-Qadir, al-Nahr, al-Durr al-Mukhtar) reinterpreted the Bazzaziyya narration as applying only to mujtahid qadis, not muqallids. For muqallids, the ruling is definitively void.
The key interpretative move: the narration is 'carried upon' (mahmool 'ala) the mujtahid.
5
Derive the mufta bihi position and its supporting reasons
Conclude that the relied-upon view is that the ruling does not take effect. Articulate the two reasons: (1) the sultan's decree prohibits weak opinions, making the qadi dismissed for that ruling; (2) the weak opinion is like nonexistent compared to the strong, so the basis of the judgment is legally null.
The passage emphasizes that even without sultanic prohibition, the weak opinion is void by consensus.

He said in al-Nahr: “What is in al-Fath must be relied upon in the madhhab, and what is in al-Bazzaziyya is interpreted as a narration from them both, so the matter becomes that this is treated like the one who forgets his madhhab, and it has passed from them both regarding the mujtahid that it is not enforceable, so the muqallid is more deserving.” End. And he said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: I say: Especially in our time, for the sultan states in his decree his prohibition of judging by weak sayings, so how about contrary to his madhhab? So he is dismissed with respect to the non-reliable of his madhhab, so his judgment in it is not enforceable, and it is voided, as elaborated in the judiciary section of al-Fath, al-Nahr and others. End. I say: And I have also known that the weak saying is like nonexistent alongside the strong, so he cannot judge by it, even if the sultan did not instruct him to judge by the strong. (4) His saying: “But what is in al-Qunyah” is a correction of what the author of al-Bahr understood from the speech of al-Bazzaziyya that if the muqallid judges by another's madhhab or by a weak narration, his judgment is enforceable. Its explanation: That the difference mentioned in al-Bazzaziyya concerns the mujtahid judge. As for the muqallid, if he judges contrary to his madhhab, it is not enforceable. This is because among the conditions for validity of judgment is that it be in accordance with the sound [opinion] of his madhhab, for two reasons: First: The sultan in his decree prohibits judging by weak sayings and obliges them to judge among people by what is sound in the madhhab, so he is dismissed with respect to the weak of his madhhab and what is outside the madhhab, and the judgment of the dismissed is absolutely invalid. Second: The weak saying in comparison to the strong is like nonexistent, so it is not for the judge to judge by it even if the sultan did not explicitly state in his decree [to judge] by the strong, because judging by what is like nonexistent is void by consensus. Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti discusses a critical rasm rule: whether a qadi who is a muqallid (follower) of the Hanafi madhhab can issue a ruling based on a weak opinion (da'if) within the madhhab or based on the opinion of another madhhab, and whether such a ruling is enforceable (nafidh). The text begins by quoting from Fath al-Qadir and Bahr al-Ra'iq, establishing that a mujtahid qadi may not judge contrary to his own ijtihad, and a muqallid qadi is appointed specifically to judge by the Hanafi madhhab, so he cannot deviate; if he does, he is considered 'azl (dismissed) for that ruling. However, the text notes a difference of opinion among the mashayikh. The view in al-Bazzaziyya (citing Sharh al-Tahawi) suggests that if a non-mujtahid qadi judges by a fatwa that later is found to be contrary to his madhhab, the ruling is enforceable and only the qadi himself may void it (according to Muhammad), while Abu Yusuf says even he cannot void it. But the passage then brings the stronger position from al-Qunyah, al-Muhit, and others, clarifying that the difference in Bazzaziyya pertains to a mujtahid qadi, not a muqallid. The relied-upon view (from Fath al-Qadir, al-Nahr, al-Durr al-Mukhtar) is that a muqallid qadi's judgment based on a weak opinion or another madhhab is not enforceable and must be annulled. Two reasons are given: First, the sultan typically instructs judges to rule only by the sound views of the madhhab, so the qadi is effectively dismissed regarding weak views. Second, a weak view is like nonexistent against the strong, so judging by it is invalid by consensus. The passage also notes that even if the sultan did not explicitly forbid weak opinions, the qadi still cannot rule by them because the weak opinion has no legal weight. This rule is especially emphasized in later times when sultans explicitly prohibit weak views. The commentary from al-Durr al-Mukhtar reinforces that the qadi is dismissed for non-reliant opinions, so his judgment is void. This is a fundamental rasm rule for muftis and qadis, clarifying the limits of a muqallid's authority.

Key Terms
المقلد (al-muqallid): A qadi who is not a mujtahid but follows a specific madhhab (Hanafi) and is appointed to judge according to that madhhab.
الضعيف (al-da'if): A weak or less authoritative opinion within the Hanafi madhhab, as opposed to the sound (sahih) or strong (rajih) view.
معزول (ma'zool): Dismissed or removed from authority; here, the qadi is considered effectively dismissed for that specific ruling because he acted outside his jurisdiction.
الراجح (al-rajih): The strong or preponderant opinion within the madhhab, which is relied upon for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the passage, what is the status of a muqallid qadi's judgment if he rules based on a weak opinion (da'if) within his madhhab?
A) It is enforceable and cannot be voided.
B) It is enforceable but only the qadi himself can void it.
C) It is not enforceable and must be annulled.
D) It is valid only if the sultan explicitly permits weak opinions.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid qadi's ruling based on a weak opinion or another madhhab is void and must be annulled, as he is appointed only to judge by the sound view of his madhhab.

The Muqallid Judge Cannot Judge by Weak or Non-Madhhab Opinions
Ruling on invalidity of muqallid's judgment based on weak opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a muqallid judge's ruling is invalid and apply the Hanafi rule that only the relied-upon (rajih) opinion may be used.

Core Idea
A muqallid judge's ruling based on a weak opinion or another madhhab is void because the weak opinion is legally non-existent.

This lesson examines a critical rule in Hanafi judicial practice: a judge who is not a mujtahid (muqallid) must strictly follow the relied-upon (rajih) opinion of his madhhab. The passage explains why deviating to a weak opinion (da'if) or to another madhhab renders his judgment void, and it clarifies the role of the ruler's decree in reinforcing this principle. Additionally, it addresses a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school about the enforcement of an erroneous ruling that coincidentally matches a mujtahid's opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors and their capacities
Distinguish between a mujtahid judge (who can independently derive rulings) and a muqallid judge (who must follow his madhhab).
2
State the general rule
The passage establishes that both types of judges cannot judge contrary to their respective authorities: the mujtahid cannot go against his own opinion, and the muqallid cannot go against his madhhab.
3
Understand the rationale for the muqallid
The weak opinion is considered legally non-existent (bimanzilat al-‘adam) compared to the preponderant (rajih), and the muqallid is not qualified for tarjih (weighting of evidence).
4
Consider the effect of the sultan's decree
If the ruler explicitly prohibits judging by weak opinions, the judge is considered dismissed (ma'zul) for that case, rendering his ruling void.
5
Analyze the exceptional dispute
Examine the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) over whether a muqallid judge's erroneous judgment that matches a mujtahid's opinion is enforceable.
The relied-upon position is that it is overturned.

Explanation of the contract of the sign of the mufti
208 It is not permissible to judge by the weak [opinion] and by the madhhab of another.
Regarding a mujtahid judge, if he judges contrary to his opinion, and the muqallid judge, if he judges contrary to his madhhab, it is not executed. End. And the muhaqqiq affirmed it in Fath al-Qadir, and his student al-Allamah Qasim in his correction.
He said in al-Nahr: "What is in al-Fath must be relied upon in the madhhab, and what is in al-Bazzaziyyah is interpreted as a transmission from them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], so the matter becomes (1) that this is considered like the one who forgot his madhhab, and it has already passed from them regarding the mujtahid that it is not executed (3), so the muqallid is more deserving." End. And he said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: I say: especially in our time, for the sultan states in his decree the prohibition of judging by weak opinions, so how about contrary to his madhhab? So he is dismissed with respect to what is not relied upon of his madhhab, so his judgment therein is not executed, and it is overturned, as detailed in the chapter of judgment in al-Fath, al-Nahr, and others. End. I say: And you have also known that the preponderated opinion is like non-existence alongside the preponderant, so he may not judge by it, even if the sultan has not explicitly ordered him to judge by the preponderant. And in Fatawa al-Allamah Qasim: "And it is not for the muqallid judge to judge by the weak; because he is not among the people of tarjih (weighting), so he should not deviate from the correct except for an unvirtuous purpose. And if he judges, it is not executed; because his judgment is a judgment without truth; because the truth is the correct. And what is transmitted that the weak opinion is strengthened by the judgment, what is meant is the judgment of the mujtahid, as clarified in its place, which does not allow this answer." End. And what he mentioned about this meaning was explicitly stated by his teacher the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir.
And this is the end of what we intended to present of reporting, clarification, and editing, with the help of Allah, the All-Knowing, the Aware. I ask Him, glorified, to make it purely for His noble face, a means of success before Him on the great day of standing, and to forgive what I have committed and perpetrated of error and sins, for He is the Mighty, the Oft-Forgiving. And praise be to Allah first and last, outwardly and inwardly. And praise be to Allah by whose grace good deeds are completed. And may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his family and companions and grant them peace. And praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.
It was completed by the pen of its compiler, the poor Muhammad Abidin, may Allah forgive him, his parents, his teachers, his offspring, and the Muslims, Amin.
And that was in the month of Rabi' al-Thani of the year 1243.
(2) His saying: "It is not executed," said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: If he judged contrary to his madhhab in error and it agreed with the opinion of a mujtahid, then it was raised to another [judge], Abu Hanifa said: he enforces it. And the two said: he overturns it; because it is an error, and error is not something subject to ijtihad. (Radd al-Muhtar 4:498)
(1) His saying: "Except for an unvirtuous purpose." Based on this, if the judge needs to judge by the weak opinion for a real and valid necessity, is it permissible for him to deviate from the correct? It needs consideration and review. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule establishing that a muqallid judge cannot issue a ruling based on a weak opinion or on the opinion of another madhhab. The author begins by distinguishing between a mujtahid judge (who may rule contrary to his own opinion if it is an error) and a muqallid judge: if the muqallid rules contrary to his madhhab, his ruling is not enforceable. This is affirmed by the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir and by Qasim. The author from al-Nahr clarifies that the ruling in al-Fath is the relied-upon position, while a statement from al-Bazzaziyyah is interpreted as a rare transmission. The muqallid is considered like one who forgot his madhhab. Al-Durr al-Mukhtar adds that in contemporary times, the ruler explicitly forbids judging by weak opinions, so ruling contrary to the madhhab renders the judge dismissed for that case; his judgment is void and can be overturned. The second reason is that the preponderated opinion is legally non-existent compared to the preponderant, so even without a ruler's decree, the judge cannot act on it. The fatwa of Qasim states that a muqallid judge is not capable of tarjih (weighting), so he must follow the correct (sahih) opinion; if he judges by a weak opinion, it is void. The claim that a weak opinion becomes strong by being acted upon applies only to a mujtahid judge. The passage concludes with a footnote: if a muqallid judge errs and rules contrary to his madhhab but coincidentally agrees with a mujtahid, Abu Hanifa says the ruling is enforced, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is overturned because it is an error. Another footnote raises the question of necessity: if a judge needs to use a weak opinion due to a real necessity, can he deviate? The author leaves it for consideration.

Key Terms
القضاء بالضعيف (al-qada' bi al-da'if): Judging based on a weak (non-reliable) opinion within the madhhab, which is not the relied-upon position.
المقلد (al-muqallid): A judge who does not have the level of ijtihad and must follow the rulings of his madhhab.
القول المرجوح (al-qawl al-marjuh): The preponderated opinion in the madhhab, considered legally non-existent in the presence of the preponderant (rajih) opinion.
منشور السلطان (manshur al-sultan): The formal decree issued by the ruler specifying that judges must rule by the correct (sahih) opinions and forbidding weak ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what happens if a muqallid judge rules by a weak opinion (against the correct view of his madhhab)?
A) The ruling is enforced if the ruler did not prohibit it.
B) The ruling is void and not executed.
C) The ruling is enforced only if it agrees with a mujtahid's opinion.
D) The ruling becomes strong and valid because the judge acted on it.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid judge must only rule by the relied-upon (rajih) opinion of his madhhab; any deviation to a weak opinion or another madhhab renders his judgment void, and the sultan's decree reinforces this prohibition.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Rule: A Judge Cannot Use Weak Opinions or Other Madhhabs
Rasm al-mufti rule with expansion and internal debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a Hanafi judge may not base a verdict on a weak opinion or another madhhab, and apply the distinction between a muqallid judge and a mujtahid regarding the validity of such a judgment.

Core Idea
A judge's use of a weak opinion or another madhhab renders the judgment unenforceable: the truth is the sahih.

A Hanafi judge is bound to the sahih (strong) opinion of his school. He is not qualified to perform tarjih between different views—that is the work of a mujtahid. Deviating from the strong opinion for anything other than a legitimate cause undermines the integrity of the judiciary. This lesson unpacks the rule, its rationale, and a key internal Hanafi difference on the consequences of a mistaken ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
State the rule: it is not permissible for a judge to judge by a weak opinion (da'if) or by the opinion of another madhhab (madhhab al-ghayr).
The rule applies to muqallid judges, not to qualified mujtahids.
2
Understand the Justification
The judge is not a person of tarjih (preference); therefore, turning away from the sahih is only done for an improper purpose (ghayr jamil). The sahih is the truth (al-haqq).
Tarjih requires independent ijtihad capacity, which a muqallid lacks.
3
Determine the Consequence of Violation
If the judge does so, the judgment is not enforceable (la yunfadhu). It is considered a judgment by other than truth.
Unenforceable means it has no legal effect and may be rescinded.
4
Address the Misconception
The claim that a weak opinion 'becomes strong' by being used in a judgment is false for a muqallid; it only applies to a mujtahid (like the founding imams).
This is a crucial distinction in Hanafi usul al-ifta.
5
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
If a judge mistakenly rules contrary to his madhhab but the ruling coincides with a mujtahid's opinion, Imam Abu Hanifa holds the judgment stands; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it must be overturned because it is a mistake.
The later relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لايجوز القضاء بالضعيف وبمذهب الغير (بالضعيف؛ لأنه ليس من أهل الترجيح فلا يعدل عن الصحيح إلا لقصد غير جميل). ولو حكم لا ينفذ؛ لأن قضاءه قضاء بغير الحق؛ لأن الحق هو الصحيح. وما نقل من أن القول الضعيف يتقوى بالقضاء، المراد به قضاء المجتهد، كما بيّن فى موضعه مما لا يحتمله هذا الجواب " . اهـ. وما ذكره من هذا المراد صرح به شيخه المحقق في فتح القدير " . وهذا آخر ما أردنا إيراده من التقرير والتوضيح والتحرير، بعون الله تعالى العليم الخبير. أسأله سبحانه أن يجعل ذلك خالصا لوجهه الكريم، موجباً للفوز لديه يوم الموقف العظيم، وأن يعفو عما جنيته واقترفته من خطأ وأوزار ، فإنه العزيز الغفّار . والحمد لله تعالى أولا وآخرا، وظاهرا وباطنا . والحمد لله الذي بنعمته تتم الصالحات. وصلى الله تعالى على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وصحبه وسلم . والحمد لله رب العالمين. نجز ذلك بقلم جامعه الفقير محمد عابدين غفر الله تعالى له ولوالديه ومشايخه وذريته والمسلمين آمين. وذلك في شهر ربيع الثاني سنة ثلاث وأربعين ومائتين وألف .
(۱) قوله : "إلا لقصد غير جميل" وعلى هذا فلو احتاج القاضي إلى الحكم بالضعيف لضرورة واقعية صحيحة معتبرة، هل يسوغ له العدول عن الصحيح؟ لينظر وليراجع. والله تعالى أعلم .
(۲) قوله : "لا ينفذ" قال في الدر المختار: إذا قضى بخلاف مذهبه غلطا ووافق قول مجتهد، ثم رفع لآخر، أمضاه عند الإمام. وقالا : ينقضه؛ لأنه غلط، والغلط ليس بمجتهد فيه . (رد المحتار : ٤٩٨/٤)
Judgment by the weak [opinion] and by the opinion of another [school] is not permissible. (By the weak because he is not a person of tarjih [preference], so he should not turn away from the correct [opinion] except for an improper intent). And if he judges, it is not executed, because his judgment is judgment by other than the truth, for the truth is the correct [opinion]. And what is transmitted that the weak saying is strengthened by judgment, its meaning is the judgment of the mujtahid, as clarified in its place in a way that this answer does not accommodate. End. And what he mentioned as this meaning was explicitly stated by his teacher the investigator in Fath al-Qadir. (1) His statement: "except for an improper intent" — and upon this, if the judge needs to judge by the weak [opinion] due to a real and valid necessity, is it permissible for him to deviate from the correct? It needs consideration and review. And Allah knows best. (2) His statement: "it is not executed" — It is said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: If he judged contrary to his madhhab mistakenly and it coincides with the saying of a mujtahid, then it is referred to another [judge]; according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], he enforces it. And the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] say: he rescinds it, because it is a mistake, and a mistake is not a matter of ijtihad. (Radd al-Muhtar, 4:498)
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule from the book 'Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' by Ibn Abidin. The text establishes a fundamental principle for judges (qudat): it is not permissible for a judge to base his judgment on a weak (da'if) opinion within his own madhhab, nor on the opinion of another madhhab (madhhab al-ghayr). The reason given for not using weak opinions is that the judge, being a muqallid (follower) in the Hanafi school, is not qualified to perform tarjih (preference between conflicting evidences). Therefore, deviating from the strong (sahih) opinion is only done for an improper motive (ghayr jamil), which is blameworthy. If a judge nonetheless does so, his judgment is not enforceable (la yunfadhu) because it is not based on the truth (al-haqq), which is the sahih position. The text addresses a common misconception: some claim that a weak opinion becomes strong when a judge rules by it. The author clarifies that this only applies to a fully qualified mujtahid (like the founding imams), not to a muqallid judge. The marginal notes expand on two points: first, whether necessity could justify using a weak opinion (footnote 1), leaving the matter open; second, the ruling if a judge mistakenly judges contrary to his own madhhab but coinciding with another mujtahid (footnote 2). Here, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the judgment is effective (amda), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it must be overturned (yanqud) because it was a mistake and mistakes are not subject to ijtihad.

Key Terms
الضعيف (al-da'if): A weak opinion within the Hanafi madhhab, i.e., one that is not sahih due to weaker evidence or conflicting with stronger proofs.
مذهب الغير (madhhab al-ghayr): The opinion of another Islamic legal school (e.g., Shafi'i, Maliki) that differs from the Hanafi position on a given issue.
لا ينفذ (la yunfadhu): The judgment is not legally enforceable; it has no binding effect and may be overturned by a subsequent judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a Hanafi judge judges by a weak opinion?
A) The judgment is valid and enforceable.
B) The judgment is not enforceable because it is based on other than the truth.
C) The judgment is valid only if the judge is a mujtahid.
D) The judgment becomes strong because of the judge's authority.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi judge must adjudicate only by the sahih (strong) opinion of his madhhab; deviating to a weak opinion or another madhhab invalidates the judgment.

Hierarchical Classification of Hanafi Jurists: The Case of 'Ali al-Razi
Biographical entry with hierarchical classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hierarchical rank of 'Ali al-Razi within the Hanafi madhhab and distinguish between the layers of muqallids (ashab al-tarjih) and mujtahids as presented in the text.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fatwa hierarchy, rank is by scholarly ability (tarjih vs. ijtihad), not by era.

This passage introduces 'Ali al-Razi, a Hanafi scholar whose classification illustrates a key principle in Usul al-Iftaa: the hierarchy of jurists. Understanding who is a muqallid capable of tarjih versus a mujtahid determines the authority of fatwa. The author also asserts a qawida (maxim) that merit, not chronology, determines rank.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar
Read the biographical details: Who was 'Ali al-Razi's teacher? From whom did he narrate? What book did he write? This establishes his credentials.
His teacher is al-Hasan ibn Ziyad; he narrated from Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.
2
Locate His Hierarchical Classification
Find the sentence where the author of al-Hidayah places him. Identify the terms used: 'first layer of muqallids' and 'people of tarjih'.
The phrase 'أولى طبقات المقلدين' directly places him.
3
Distinguish the Two Layers
List the scholars mentioned as mujtahids (e.g., al-Khassaf, al-Tahawi) and as muqallids (e.g., al-Quduri, author of al-Hidayah). Note the criteria: tarjih vs. ijtihad.
Mujtahids can derive rulings; muqallids can only prefer between transmitted opinions.
4
Apply the Qawida
Read the maxim 'مراتب الرجال بالفضل والكمال، لا بتقادم الأزمنة والآجال'. Understand how it justifies including later scholars like Ibn Kamal in the first muqallid layer.
This maxim overrides any assumption that earlier scholars are automatically higher.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على الرازي : عن الصميرى : أنه من أقران محمد بن شجاع، وكان عارفًا بمذهب أصحابنا، وطعن في مسائل من الأصول فى زهد وورع وسخاء، أخذ الفقه عن الحسن بن زياد، وروى عن محمد وأبي يوسف. وله كتاب الصلاة، وعده صاحب الهداية من أولى طبقات المقلدين وهم أصحاب الترجيح مثل : أبي الحسن القدوري، وصاحب الهداية وأمثالهما، دون طبقة المجتهدين كالخصاف، والطحاوي، والكرخي والسرخسي، والحلواني، وقاضيخان، وصاحب الذخيرة، وصاحب الخلاصة. وظني أن المولى شمس الدين أحمد بن كمال ملحق بهم، بل المولى الفاضل أبو السعود العمادي أيضا ؛ فإن مراتب الرجال بالفضل والكمال، لا بتقادم الأزمنة والآجال، كذا في الفوائد البهية .
'Ali al-Razi: From al-Samiri: He was a contemporary of Muhammad ibn Shuja', and he was knowledgeable in the madhhab of our companions. He criticized some issues of principles (usul) while being ascetic, pious, and generous. He took fiqh from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and narrated from Muhammad and Abu Yusuf. He has a book on prayer (Kitab al-Salat). The author of al-Hidayah counted him among the first of the layers of muqallids, who are the people of tarjih (preference), such as Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri, the author of al-Hidayah, and their peers, not the layer of mujtahids like al-Khassaf, al-Tahawi, al-Karkhi, al-Sarakhsi, al-Halwani, Qadikhan, the author of al-Dhakhira, and the author of al-Khulasa. I think that Mawla Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn Kamal is attached to them, even the virtuous Mawla Abu al-Su'ud al-'Imadi also; for the ranks of men are by virtue and perfection, not by the passage of time and terms, as in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for 'Ali al-Razi, a Hanafi scholar known for his knowledge of the madhhab and his criticism of some usul issues. The text classifies him within the Hanafi hierarchy of jurists: he belongs to the first layer of muqallids (أولى طبقات المقلدين) — those capable of tarjih (preference between transmitted opinions) — as opposed to the higher layer of mujtahids (المجتهدين) who can derive rulings independently. This classification is crucial in Usul al-Iftaa for understanding the authority of fatwa: a muqallid mutlaq (like the author of al-Hidayah) can weigh transmitted opinions, but a mujtahid (like al-Tahawi) can derive new rulings. The author adds his own opinion that later scholars like Ibn Kamal and Abu al-Su'ud al-'Imadi should be ranked similarly, emphasizing that rank is by merit, not era. The entry is incomplete; it cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
طبقات المقلدين (tabaqat al-muqallidin): The layers of jurists who are not independent mujtahids but can weigh and prefer between existing Hanafi opinions (tarjih).
أصحاب الترجيح (ashab al-tarjih): Those who have the ability to prefer one transmission over another within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which scholars are considered mujtahids (not muqallids)?
A) Al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah
B) Al-Khassaf, al-Tahawi, al-Karkhi
C) 'Ali al-Razi and Ibn Kamal
D) Al-Halwani and Abu al-Su'ud

Key Takeaway
The passage establishes that within the Hanafi school, the hierarchy of jurists is based on intellectual capability (ijtihad vs. tarjih), not era, and that a muqallid with tarjih ability holds a distinct rank below mujtahids.
