Definition and Conditions of the Muqayyad Mujtahid
Al-Nawawi defines the second type of mufti: the restricted mujtahid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the muqayyad mujtahid, list his conditions, and explain the authority of his fatwa and the nature of taqlid for his followers.

Core Idea
A muqayyad mujtahid derives rulings within his imam’s framework; his fatwa is authoritative, but taqlid is to the imam.

Imam al-Nawawi describes the second type of mufti: the restricted mujtahid. This scholar works within the boundaries of his imam's principles, lacking some tools of the absolute mujtahid. Understanding this rank is crucial for grasping the mufti hierarchy and the practice of taqlid. In this lesson, we will parse the definition, conditions, and the legal effect of his fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term: muqayyad mujtahid
Locate the term in the passage and note its Arabic (مجتهد مقيد). Understand that it refers to a mujtahid restricted to the madhhab of his imam.
The text also uses 'al-mujtahid fi al-madhhab' in the footnote.
2
Break down the definition elements
Extract the three defining characteristics: (a) independent in establishing the imam's principles with evidence, (b) does not go beyond the imam's principles and rules, (c) lacks some tools of the absolute mujtahid (e.g., hadith or Arabic mastery).
The text says 'لا يعرى عن شوب تقليد' indicating a tint of taqlid due to these lacks.
3
List the conditions
From the passage, identify the required qualifications: knowledge of fiqh, usul al-fiqh, detailed evidences; insight into analogies and meanings; full practice in takhrij and istinbat; ability to append new cases to the imam's principles.
These conditions distinguish him from a mere muqallid.
4
Determine the legal effect
The text states that his fatwa is like that of the independent mujtahid in practice, and it counts in ijma' and ikhtilaf. The follower is a muqallid of the imam, not of the restricted mujtahid himself.
This underscores the authority of the fatwa while preserving taqlid to the imam.
5
Situate in the hierarchy
Connect to the concept of 'as-hab al-wujuh' (people of the accepted faces) and examples from the Hanafi school: al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, al-Karkhi, al-Tahawi. Understand that this rank is recognized across madhhabs.
The footnote provides cross-madhhab examples.

Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi. 24. Then the fatwa of the mufti in this case is like the fatwa of the independent (mujtahid) in terms of acting upon it and considering it in consensus and disagreement. 25. The second case: that he be a restricted mujtahid in the madhhab of his imam, independent in establishing his principles with evidence, except that he does not go beyond in his evidences the principles and rules of his imam. His condition is that he be knowledgeable of fiqh and its principles and the detailed evidences of rulings, insightful into the methods of analogies and meanings, fully practiced in derivation and deduction, capable of appending to his imam's principles what is not explicitly stated. And he is not free from a tint of taqlid towards him, due to his lack of some tools of the independent, by lacking in hadith or Arabic, and often the restricted one lacked them. 26. Then he takes the texts of his imam as principles from which he derives, like the action of the independent with the texts of the Shariah. And perhaps he suffices in the ruling with the evidence of his imam and does not seek a contradictory, like the action of the independent with texts. And this is the description of our companions, the people of 'wujuh', and upon it were the imams of our companions or most of them. 27. And the one acting upon the fatwa of this (mufti) is a muqallid of his imam, not of him. 28. Then the apparent meaning of the words of the companions is that from this state, the obligation (of seeking knowledge?) is not fulfilled. (Footnotes) (1) His statement: 'That he be a restricted mujtahid' and it is called the restricted mujtahid or the mujtahid within the madhhab. That is, he is restricted to the madhhab of his imam, independent in establishing his principles with evidence and deriving details upon them in detail, except that he does not go beyond what his imam held in fundamentals and branches, like al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, al-Karkhi, and al-Tahawi from the Hanafis, al-Abhari and Ibn Abi Zayd from the Malikis, Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi and al-Marwazi from the Shafi'is, and others like them from the people of the accepted 'wujuh' in the madhhab, deducing from the imam's texts. This is the rank of ijtihad within the madhhab. (2) His statement: 'principles from which he derives' means he derives rulings for incidents for which there is no text from the imam of the madhhab by way of deduction from the texts or rules transmitted from the imam. (3) His statement: 'the people of wujuh' is one whose statement and deduction is considered a 'wajh' in the madhhab, so the meaning is: the people of the accepted 'wujuh' in the madhhab, and they are also called the people of takhrij.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage from Imam al-Nawawi's 'Adab al-Fatwa' defines the second type of mufti: the restricted mujtahid (al-mujtahid al-muqayyad). This scholar is independent in establishing the principles of his imam (e.g., Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi‘i) using evidence, but he does not go beyond those principles. He must be deeply learned in fiqh, usul al-fiqh, and the detailed evidences, skilled in analogy and meaning, practiced in deduction, and able to extend rulings to new cases by referring to his imam's principles. However, he lacks some tools of the absolute mujtahid, such as full mastery of hadith or Arabic, so his work is tinged with taqlid. He treats his imam's texts as the independent mujtahid treats the primary sources of Shariah. The fatwa of such a mufti is considered valid for practice and counts in consensus and disagreement, just like that of an independent mujtahid. The one who follows his fatwa is considered a muqallid of the imam, not of the restricted mujtahid himself. The passage also introduces the concept of 'as-hab al-wujuh' (people of the accepted faces), who are those whose deductions are recognized as authoritative within the madhhab. The footnotes provide additional clarification: examples of such mujtahids include al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, al-Karkhi, and al-Tahawi among Hanafis, and they explain that deduction (takhrij) is the method used for cases not explicitly covered by the imam's texts. This lesson thus defines a key rank in the mufti hierarchy and outlines the conditions for this level of ijtihad.

Key Terms
مجتهد مقيد (mujtahid muqayyad): A mujtahid who is restricted to the madhhab of his imam, independent in establishing the imam's principles but not going beyond them, lacking some tools of the absolute mujtahid.
أصحاب الوجوه (as-hab al-wujuh): The people whose opinions and deductions are considered authoritative 'faces' (wujuh) within the madhhab; they are also called 'as-hab al-takhrij' (people of deduction).
تخريج (takhrij): The process of deriving rulings for new cases by analogy or inference from the texts or rules of the imam, when no explicit text exists from the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a layperson follows the fatwa of a muqayyad mujtahid, who is the actual object of taqlid?
A) The muqayyad mujtahid himself.
B) The founding imam of the madhhab (e.g., Abu Hanifa).
C) The early scholars of the first generation.
D) The consensus of all mujtahids.

Key Takeaway
The muqayyad mujtahid operates within his imam's framework, and his fatwa carries the same weight as that of an absolute mujtahid in practice, but taqlid is to the founding imam.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
The Muqayyad Mufti: Standing in Place of the Imam
Rasm rule: muqayyad mufti authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a muqayyad mufti's fatwa fulfills the communal obligation and identify that the mustafti is following the imam.

Core Idea
A bound mufti stands in the place of his imam, fulfilling fard kifaya when basing rulings on the school's principles.

This passage from al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa addresses a critical question: can a mufti who is not an absolute mujtahid fulfill the communal obligation of delivering fatwa? The answer is yes, on the condition that he acts as a substitute for his independent imam and derives rulings from the imam's usul. This lesson parses the definition and authority of the muqayyad mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Locate the terms 'muqayyad', 'fard kifaya', and 'mustafti' in the Arabic text. Understand their definitions as given in the key terms.
The muqayyad mufti is not an absolute mujtahid but is bound to his imam.
2
Analyze the fulfillment of fard kifaya
Examine the statement: 'It appears that the obligation is fulfilled through it in fatwa, even if not in reviving the sciences.' Why does the muqayyad's fatwa count for fard kifaya? Because he stands in the place of his independent imam.
Footnote 1 explains the communal obligation in detail: in the absence of absolute mujtahids, the muqayyad must step in.
3
Determine the mustafti's taqlid
The text explicitly states that when the mufti issues a fatwa via takhrij, the mustafti is following the imam, not the mufti. This is a key principle in rasm al-mufti.
Imam al-Haramayn emphasizes this point in al-Ghiyathi.
4
Apply the legal definition
Use the legal_definition_dissector to see the components of the muqayyad's authority: hukm, mahall, sabab, shart, mani, athar. How do these condition his role?
The shart: he must base rulings on his imam's principles.

Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi. (The sufficiency). Abu Amr said: It appears that the obligation is fulfilled through it in fatwa, even if it is not fulfilled in reviving the sciences from which fatwa is derived; because he stands in the place of his independent imam. As a branch on the correct view, and it is the permissibility of taqlid of the deceased. Then the bound one may be independent in a specific issue or chapter, as previously mentioned. And he may issue a fatwa in what has no text from his imam, by deriving it from his principles. This is the correct view upon which practice is based, and it is the recourse of muftis for long periods. Then if he issues a fatwa by his derivation, the mustafti is following his imam, not him. This is what Imam al-Haramayn cut with in his book 'al-Ghiyathi', and how abundant are its benefits! Footnote 1: His saying: 'The communal obligation is not fulfilled by it, and its aspect: that what is in it of taqlid is a deficiency and defect in the objective. We have mentioned from Imam al-Baghawi that the communal obligation is to learn what reaches one to the level of ijtihad and the place of fatwa and judgment, which is the rank of the absolute independent mufti. But when the absolute independent mujtahid is absent, then the least is that they should learn the religion so that in every region there is one who can extract the ruling of incidents and be an intermediary between Allah and His servants in what they need of learning the rulings of His Sharia, otherwise they all sin.' Footnote 2: His saying: 'The permissibility of taqlid of the deceased.' Is it permissible for the living to taqlid the deceased and act by his fatwa without considering it by the evidence that makes acting by it valid? There are two opinions among the followers of Imam Ahmad and al-Shafi'i. The one who forbids said: His ijtihad could change if he were alive; for he would renew his consideration upon the occurrence of this incident, either obligatorily or preferably, according to the well-known dispute, and perhaps if he renewed his consideration he would retract his first statement. The second: permissibility, and upon it is the practice of all muqallids in the lands of the earth, and the best of what they have of taqlid is taqlid of the dead. The one who forbids taqlid of the deceased among them only says it with his tongue, but his practice in his fatwas and judgments is contrary to it. Statements do not die with the death of their speakers, just as reports do not die with the death of their narrators and transmitters. See: I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in 4/215. The full discussion will come. Footnote 3: His saying: 'As previously mentioned' is an indication to the permissibility of partial ijtihad, and the investigation has passed in detail at the end of the first section. Footnote 4: His saying: 'In his book al-Ghiyathi' it is by Imam Abd al-Malik ibn Abd Allah al-Juwayni, known as Imam.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage from al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa presents several rasm al-mufti rules. It begins by addressing the fulfillment of the communal obligation (fard kifaya) through the fatwa of a bound mufti (muqayyad) who stands in place of his independent imam. The main text then branches into the established ruling that taqlid of a deceased imam is permissible. The footnote elaborates the two opinions among Hanbalis and Shafi'is: one forbidding it due to the possibility of ijtihad change, the other permitting it, which is the actual practice of all muqallids. The text then states that a muqayyad mufti can gain independence in a specific issue or chapter, and he may issue fatwas when there is no explicit text from his imam by deriving rulings based on his imam's principles (usul). This is the correct and operative view. Finally, it establishes that when a mufti issues a fatwa using his own derivation (takhrij), the mustafti (seeker of fatwa) is actually taqliding the imam, not the mufti himself—a point emphatically stated by Imam al-Haramayn. Footnotes further clarify the concept of partial ijtihad and identify the book referenced.

Key Terms
المقيد (al-muqayyad): A mufti who is not an absolute mujtahid but is bound to his imam's school; he may become independent in specific issues or chapters.
التخريج (al-takhrij): Deriving a ruling from the principles of the imam when there is no explicit text.
المستفتى (al-mustafti): The person seeking a fatwa; he is a muqallid of the imam, not the mufti who only conveys the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the fatwa of a muqayyad mufti fulfill the communal obligation (fard kifaya)?
A) Because he is an absolute mujtahid.
B) Because he stands in the place of his independent imam.
C) Because he does not rely on taqlid.
D) Because the mustafti follows him.

Key Takeaway
The muqayyad mufti's fatwa is valid and fulfills fard kifaya, and the mustafti follows the imam, not the mufti.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Taqlid of the Deceased and the Muqayyad's Takhrij
Rasm rule: taqlid of deceased and takhrij

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the permissibility of taqlid of a deceased imam and describe how a muqayyad mufti can derive rulings (takhrij) when no explicit text exists.

Core Idea
Taqlid of a deceased imam is permissible and practiced universally; a muqayyad mufti may derive rulings from his imam's principles.

One of the most debated issues in fatwa methodology is whether a living person may follow the ruling of a deceased mujtahid. Al-Nawawi presents the position that it is permissible, and that in practice, all muqallids do so. He also addresses the muqayyad mufti's ability to perform takhrij, which enables him to handle new cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute on taqlid of the deceased
In footnote 2, two opinions are mentioned among the followers of Ahmad and al-Shafi'i. One forbids it due to possible change of ijtihad, the other permits it, which is the practice of all muqallids.
The text strongly endorses permissibility: statements do not die.
2
Understand the muqayyad's takhrij authority
The text states: 'He may issue a fatwa in what has no text from his imam, by deriving it from his principles.' This is takhrij, a legitimate method for a bound mufti.
This is the correct view upon which practice is based.
3
Trace the mustafti's taqlid in takhrij cases
Even when the mufti uses his own derivation, the mustafti is taqliding the imam, not the mufti. This is cut by Imam al-Haramayn.
The mufti is merely a conveyor; the authority remains with the imam.
4
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Given a modern issue with no explicit text, a muqayyad mufti can use takhrij. His fatwa is valid and the mustafti follows the imam.
This principle ensures continuity of fatwa in the absence of absolute mujtahids.

(۱) قوله : "لا يتأدى به فرض الكفاية ووجهه : أن ما فيه من التقليد، نقص وخلل في المقصود، وقد ذكرنا عن الإمام البغوى أن فرض الكفاية أن يتعلم ما يبلغ به رتبة الاجتهاد ومحل الفتوى والقضاء، وهو رتبة المفتى المطلق المستقل، لكن لما عدم المجتهد المطلق المستقل فلا أقل من أن يقوموا بتعلم الدين حتى يكون في كل ناحية من يقدر على استخراج حكم الحوادث ويكون واسطة بين الله وعباده في ما يحتاجون إليه من تعلم أحكام شريعته، وإلا عصوا جميعاً.
(۲) قوله : جواز تقليد الميت" هل يجوز للحى تقليد الميت والعمل بفتواه من غير اعتبارها بالدليل الموجب بصحة العمل بها؟ فيه وجهان لأصحاب الإمام أحمد والشافعي، فمن منعه قال : يجوز تغيير اجتهاده لو كان حيا ؛ فإنه كان يجدد النظر عند نزول هذه النازلة إما وجوبًا وإما استحباباً ، على النزاع المشهور، ولعله لو جدّد النظر لرجع عن قوله الأول والثاني : الجواز، وعليه عمل جميع المقلدين في أقطار الأرض، وخيار ما بأيديهم من التقليد تقليد الأموات، ومن منع منهم تقليد الميت فإنما هو شيء يقوله بلسانه، وعمله في فتاويه وأحكامه بخلافه، والأقوال لا تموت بموت قائلها، كما لا تموت الأخبار بموت رواها وناقليها . راجع : إعلام الموقعين : ٤ / ٢١٥ . وسيأتي تمام الكلام عليه .
(۳) قوله : "كما تقدم إشارة إلى جواز تجزئ الاجتهاد، وقد مر البحث مفصلا في آخر القسم الأول.
(٤) قوله : " في كتابه الغياثي " هو للإمام عبد الملك بن عبد الله الجويني، المعروف بإمام
Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi. (The sufficiency). Abu Amr said: It appears that the obligation is fulfilled through it in fatwa, even if it is not fulfilled in reviving the sciences from which fatwa is derived; because he stands in the place of his independent imam. As a branch on the correct view, and it is the permissibility of taqlid of the deceased. Then the bound one may be independent in a specific issue or chapter, as previously mentioned. And he may issue a fatwa in what has no text from his imam, by deriving it from his principles. This is the correct view upon which practice is based, and it is the recourse of muftis for long periods. Then if he issues a fatwa by his derivation, the mustafti is following his imam, not him. This is what Imam al-Haramayn cut with in his book 'al-Ghiyathi', and how abundant are its benefits! Footnote 1: His saying: 'The communal obligation is not fulfilled by it, and its aspect: that what is in it of taqlid is a deficiency and defect in the objective. We have mentioned from Imam al-Baghawi that the communal obligation is to learn what reaches one to the level of ijtihad and the place of fatwa and judgment, which is the rank of the absolute independent mufti. But when the absolute independent mujtahid is absent, then the least is that they should learn the religion so that in every region there is one who can extract the ruling of incidents and be an intermediary between Allah and His servants in what they need of learning the rulings of His Sharia, otherwise they all sin.' Footnote 2: His saying: 'The permissibility of taqlid of the deceased.' Is it permissible for the living to taqlid the deceased and act by his fatwa without considering it by the evidence that makes acting by it valid? There are two opinions among the followers of Imam Ahmad and al-Shafi'i. The one who forbids said: His ijtihad could change if he were alive; for he would renew his consideration upon the occurrence of this incident, either obligatorily or preferably, according to the well-known dispute, and perhaps if he renewed his consideration he would retract his first statement. The second: permissibility, and upon it is the practice of all muqallids in the lands of the earth, and the best of what they have of taqlid is taqlid of the dead. The one who forbids taqlid of the deceased among them only says it with his tongue, but his practice in his fatwas and judgments is contrary to it. Statements do not die with the death of their speakers, just as reports do not die with the death of their narrators and transmitters. See: I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in 4/215. The full discussion will come. Footnote 3: His saying: 'As previously mentioned' is an indication to the permissibility of partial ijtihad, and the investigation has passed in detail at the end of the first section. Footnote 4: His saying: 'In his book al-Ghiyathi' it is by Imam Abd al-Malik ibn Abd Allah al-Juwayni, known as Imam.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage from al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa presents several rasm al-mufti rules. It begins by addressing the fulfillment of the communal obligation (fard kifaya) through the fatwa of a bound mufti (muqayyad) who stands in place of his independent imam. The main text then branches into the established ruling that taqlid of a deceased imam is permissible. The footnote elaborates the two opinions among Hanbalis and Shafi'is: one forbidding it due to the possibility of ijtihad change, the other permitting it, which is the actual practice of all muqallids. The text then states that a muqayyad mufti can gain independence in a specific issue or chapter, and he may issue fatwas when there is no explicit text from his imam by deriving rulings based on his imam's principles (usul). This is the correct and operative view. Finally, it establishes that when a mufti issues a fatwa using his own derivation (takhrij), the mustafti (seeker of fatwa) is actually taqliding the imam, not the mufti himself—a point emphatically stated by Imam al-Haramayn. Footnotes further clarify the concept of partial ijtihad and identify the book referenced.

Key Terms
المقيد (al-muqayyad): A mufti who is not an absolute mujtahid but is bound to his imam's school; he may become independent in specific issues or chapters.
التخريج (al-takhrij): Deriving a ruling from the principles of the imam when there is no explicit text.
المستفتى (al-mustafti): The person seeking a fatwa; he is a muqallid of the imam, not the mufti who only conveys the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the permissibility of taqlid of a deceased imam?
A) The living mufti's opinion supersedes the deceased's.
B) Statements do not die with their speakers, just as reports do not die with their narrators.
C) The deceased imam's writings are more reliable.
D) It is allowed only in matters of worship.

Key Takeaway
Taqlid of a deceased imam is permitted and is the normal practice; a muqayyad mufti can derive rulings via takhrij, and the mustafti follows the imam.

Attribution of Derived Opinions (Qawl Mukharraj)
Definition and ruling on attributing derived opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct attribution of a derived opinion (qawl mukharraj) and apply the rule that it is attributed to the imam in a qualified manner, not absolutely.

Core Idea
A derived opinion is attributed to the imam in a qualified manner, not absolutely, to avoid confusion with explicit texts.

This lesson examines a key rule of rasm al-mufti: how to attribute an opinion derived from the imam's texts or principles when the imam did not rule on the exact issue. The correct view, as explained by al-Nawawi, distinguishes between absolute and qualified attribution, preserving the integrity of the school's transmitted texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two derivation methods
The text states a mufti either derives from a specific text (nass) of the imam, or from his principles (usul) when no text exists. Identify these two scenarios.
This shows the basis of takhrij.
2
Understand the dispute on attribution
The passage quotes a dispute: can a derived opinion be attributed to the imam? Recognize that there are differing views.
The dispute is between absolute, qualified, or no attribution.
3
Grasp the correct ruling (qualified attribution)
The correct view (al-asahh) is that it is not attributed absolutely, but only in a qualified manner as 'mukharraj' (derived). Note the reason: to avoid confusion with manqul (explicit texts).
This is the operative rule for fatwa.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a derived opinion, determine how you would attribute it to the imam in a fatwa. Use the qualification: 'this is derived from the imam's principles'.
Practice ensures correct usage in real fatwas.

Source Text

آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى

قال الشيخ أبو عمرو : وينبغى أن يخرج هذا على خلاف حكاه الشيخ أبو إسحاق الشيرازي وغيره أن ما يخرجه أصحابنا هل يجوز نسبته إلى الشافعي؟ والأصح أنه لا ينسب إليه).
۳۲ - ثم تارةً يخرج من نص معين لإمامه، وتارة لا يجده فيخرج على
أصوله ، بأن يجد دليلا على شرط ما يحتج به إمامه ، فيفتى بموجبه . ۳۳ - فإن نص إمامه على شيء، ونص (۲) في مسألة تشبهها على خلافه، فخرج من أحدهما إلى الآخر (۳)، سمّى "قولا مخرجا ".
(۱) قوله : "والأصح أنه لا ينسب إليه أى مطلقا وأما مقيدا فيجوز، وهذا لإظهار الفرق بين المنصوص والمخرج . قال شيخ الإسلام أبو يحيى زكريا الأنصاري الشافعي: " فإن لم يعرف للمجتهد قول في مسألة، لكن يعرف له قول (في نظيرها، فهو أى قوله في نظيرها . (قوله المخرج فيها على الأصح أى خرجه الأصحاب فيها إلحاقا لها بنظيرها ، وقيل : ليس قولا له فيها؛ لاحتمال أن يذكر فرقا بين المسألتين لو روجع في ذلك . ( والأصح ) على الأول (لا ينسب) القول فيها إليه مطلقا، بل ينسب إليه (مقيدا) بأنّه محرج، حتى لا يلتبس بالمنصوص، وقيل: لا حاجة إلى تقييده ؛ لأنه جعل قوله " .
غاية الوصول شرح لب الأصول، ص : ١٤١ . وراجع أيضا "شرح اللمع " : ٢/ . ١٠٨٤ ، ١٠٨٥ ، دار العرب الإسلامي)
(۲) قوله : "نص " أى الإمام، وقوله : "نصيه " أي نصى الإمام .
(۳) قوله : "فخرج من أحدهما إلى الآخر " إذا أفتى المجتهد في مسألتين متشابهتين بحكمين مختلفين في وقتين، فهل يجوز نقل الحكم وتخريجه من كل واحدة منهما إلى الأخرى أو لا ؟ قال بعض الشافعية رضى الله عنهم: يجوز نقل الحكم في كل واحدة من المسألتين إلى الأخرى وتخريجهما على قولين، واحتجوا بما تقرر عند الشافعية في الأصول من وجوب حمل المطلق على المقيد وإن كانا في حادثتين ،
Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi. Sheikh Abu Amr said: This should be derived from a dispute narrated by Sheikh Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi and others: 'Whether what our companions derive is permissible to attribute to al-Shafi'i?' The correct view is that it is not attributed to him. Then sometimes he derives from a specific text of his imam, and sometimes he does not find it, so he derives from his principles, by finding evidence on a condition of what his imam uses as proof, so he issues a fatwa accordingly. If his imam has a text on something, and a text (2) in a similar issue contrary to it, then he derives from one to the other (3), it is called 'a derived statement'. Footnote 1: His saying: 'The correct view is that it is not attributed to him absolutely. But in a qualified manner, it is permissible. This is to show the difference between the textually stated and the derived. Sheikh al-Islam Abu Yahya Zakariyya al-Ansari al-Shafi'i said: 'If the mujtahid's statement is not known in a matter, but his statement is known in its analogue, then it is his statement in the analogue. (His statement) the derived opinion in it, according to the correct view, means the companions derived it in it by analogy to its analogue. And it is said: it is not a statement for him in it, because of the possibility that he might mention a difference between the two matters if he were consulted. (The correct view) on the first: (it is not attributed) the statement in it to him absolutely, rather it is attributed to him (qualified) as derived, so that it is not confused with the textually stated. And it is said: there is no need for this qualification because he made it his statement.' Ghayat al-Wusul sharh Lubb al-Usul p.141. And also see: Sharh al-Lum' 2/1084-1085, Dar al-Arab al-Islami. Footnote 2: His saying: 'text' i.e., the imam's text; and his saying: 'nasayhi' meaning the imam's two texts. Footnote 3: His saying: 'then he derived from one to the other' if the mujtahid issues fatwas in two similar issues with two different rulings at two different times, is it permissible to transfer the ruling and derive from each of them to the other or not? Some Shafi'is, may Allah be pleased with them, said: it is permissible to transfer the ruling in each of the two issues to the other and derive them as two opinions. They argued with what is established among the Shafi'is in usul, that it is obligatory to apply the absolute to the restricted even if they are in two incidents.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage continues the rasm al-mufti discussion from al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa. Sheikh Abu Amr points to a dispute: when a mufti derives an opinion based on his imam's principles, can it be attributed to the imam? The correct view is that it cannot be attributed absolutely, but it can be attributed in a qualified manner (as a derived opinion). The text then describes two methods of derivation: from a specific text of the imam, or from his general principles (usul) when no explicit text exists. A specific case is defined: if the imam has two texts on similar issues that are contradictory, and the mufti derives from one to the other, that is called a 'qawl mukharraj' (derived statement). The footnote elaborates that this derived opinion is not attributed to the imam absolutely but only qualifiedly, to avoid confusion with textually stated (manqul) opinions. The footnote also cites Zakariyya al-Ansari's discussion on analogical derivation. Another footnote addresses the sub-issue of whether it is permissible to transfer rulings from one similar issue to another if the imam gave different rulings in two similar cases; some Shafi'is allow it, arguing from the necessity of applying the absolute to the restricted across incidents.

Key Terms
قول مخرج (qawl mukharraj): A ruling derived by a mufti from the imam's texts or principles, not explicitly stated by the imam; it is attributed to the imam in a qualified manner (mukharraj).
منصوص (manqul): A ruling explicitly stated by the imam in his texts.
تخريج (takhrij): The process of deriving a ruling from the imam's principles when no explicit text exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How is a 'qawl mukharraj' attributed to the imam according to the correct view in this passage?
A) Absolutely, as if the imam said it
B) It is not attributed at all
C) In a qualified manner, as derived
D) Only if there is consensus

Key Takeaway
A derived opinion (qawl mukharraj) is attributed to the imam in a qualified manner, not absolutely, to preserve the distinction from explicit texts.

Rules of Takhreej (Extrapolation) in Fatwa: Definition, Types, and Dispute
Explains the definition, types, conditions, and dispute regarding takhreej in fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of takhreej, state their conditions, and apply the Hanafi rule regarding attribution of extrapolated rulings.

Core Idea
Takhreej allows deriving rulings from the Imam's texts or principles, but attribution to the Imam is only qualified, not absolute.

This passage from Imam al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa introduces the concept of takhreej—extrapolating rulings for new cases from the Imam's works. As a mufti, knowing when and how to derive rulings from the Imam's texts or principles is essential, but equally important is understanding how to attribute those rulings correctly. The Hanafi school has a parallel methodology that emphasizes clarity in attribution to avoid confusion between direct and derived opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of takhreej
Locate where the text defines takhreej as deriving a ruling from a specific text of the Imam or from his principles (usul). Note the two distinct sources.
The term 'takhreej' here is used in the Shafi'i context, but the Hanafi school uses similar terminology.
2
Distinguish between the two types
Parse the text to see: Type 1 is extraction from an explicit text on a similar case; Type 2 is extraction from the Imam's established principles when no explicit text exists.
The first type yields a 'qawl mukharraj'; the second yields a 'wajh' if it differs from some companions.
3
Understand the condition for Type 1
The condition is that no distinction (farq) exists between the two texts. If a distinction is possible, the rulings remain separate. This is critical for valid extrapolation.
4
Follow the dispute on attribution
The text presents a Shafi'i internal debate: can an extrapolated ruling be attributed to the Imam? The sound opinion says only with qualification (mukharraj).
Hanafis similarly qualify attribution, using terms like 'mukharraj' or 'wajh' to indicate the ruling is derived, not direct.
5
Apply the Hanafi rule
In the Hanafi madhhab, takhreej is a standard method for later scholars, but the ruling is always attributed to the Imam's methodology, not the Imam himself. The mufti must state it as derived from usul.
This prevents confusion between manqul (transmitted) rulings and mukharraj (derived) ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ أبو عمرو : وينبغى أن يخرج هذا على خلاف حكاه الشيخ أبو إسحاق الشيرازي وغيره أن ما يخرجه أصحابنا هل يجوز نسبته إلى الشافعي؟ والأصح أنه لا ينسب إليه). ۳۲ - ثم تارةً يخرج من نص معين لإمامه، وتارة لا يجده فيخرج على أصوله ، بأن يجد دليلا على شرط ما يحتج به إمامه ، فيفتى بموجبه . ۳۳ - فإن نص إمامه على شيء، ونص (۲) في مسألة تشبهها على خلافه، فخرج من أحدهما إلى الآخر (۳)، سمّى "قولا مخرجا " . الحرمين، المتوفى سنة ٤٧٨ هـ ثمان وسبعين وأربعمائة صنّفه للوزير غياث الدين نظام الملك ؛ لأجل ذلك سماه " الغياثي " ، سلك فيه غالبا مسلك الأحكام السلطانية، وله كتاب " غياث الأم في الإمامة. راجع : كشف الظنون : ۲/ ۱۲۱۳ . ( والأصح ) على الأول (لا ينسب) القول فيها إليه مطلقا، بل ينسب إليه (مقيدا) بأنّه محرج، حتى لا يلتبس بالمنصوص، وقيل: لا حاجة إلى تقييده ؛ لأنه جعل قوله " . غاية الوصول شرح لب الأصول، ص : ١٤١ . وراجع أيضا "شرح اللمع " : ٢/ . ١٠٨٤ ، ١٠٨٥ ، دار العرب الإسلامي) (۲) قوله : "نص " أى الإمام، وقوله : "نصيه " أي نصى الإمام . (۳) قوله : "فخرج من أحدهما إلى الآخر " إذا أفتى المجتهد في مسألتين متشابهتين بحكمين مختلفين في وقتين، فهل يجوز نقل الحكم وتخريجه من كل واحدة منهما إلى الأخرى أو لا ؟ قال بعض الشافعية رضى الله عنهم: يجوز نقل الحكم في كل واحدة من المسألتين إلى الأخرى وتخريجهما على قولين، واحتجوا بما تقرر عند الشافعية في الأصول من وجوب حمل المطلق على المقيد وإن كانا في حادثتين ، آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى ٣٤ (۱) وشرط هذا التخريج (١) أن لا يجد بين نصيه ،فرقا، فإن وجده وجب تقريرهما على ظاهرهما . ويختلفون كثيراً في القول بالتخريج في مثل ذلك ؛ لاختلافهم في إمكان الفرق . قلت : وأكثر ذلك يمكن فيه الفرق وقد ذكروه . :وقالوا : إن الله تعالى لما نص فى كفارة القتل على الإيمان، وأطلق في كفارة الظهار قسنا إحداهما على الأخرى واعتبرنا الإيمان فيهما ، كذلك ههنا . وقال آخرون : لا يجوز؛ لأنه لم ينص في كل واحدة منهما إلا على قول، فلايجوز أن ينسب إليه ما لم ينص عليه . والآن الظاهر أنه قصد الفرق بين المسألتين، فمن جمع بينهما فقد خالفه . والجواب عن احتجاجهم : إن هناك قيد في إحدى الموضعين وأطلق في الآخر، فحملنا المطلق على المقيد ، بخلاف مسألتنا فإنه نص فى كل واحدة من المسألتين على حكم بخلاف ما نص على الأخرى، فلا يجوز القياس مع التصريح بالخلاف، وصار وزان مسألتنا الصوم في كفارة التمتع مع الصوم في كفارة القتل والظهار ؛ فإنه لما نص في الظهار والقتل على التتابع ونص فى التمتع على التفريق، لم يجز اعتبار أحدهما ،بالآخر، فأما إذا نص في مسألة على حكم ونص في غيرها على حكم يخالفه ولا يمكن الفصل بين المسألتين بوجه فلا خلاف أن جوابه في إحداهما ينقل إلى الأخرى، ويخرجان على قولين ويكون حكمهما حكم مسألة واحدة نص فيها على قولين . والصحيح هو القول الثاني كما صرح به في شرح اللمع : ص ۱۰۸۳ ، والتبصرة، . للشيخ الإمام أبي إسحاق إبراهيم بن على الشيرازي: ص٥١٦ . (۱) قوله : " وشرط هذا التخريج " أى شرط النوع الأول من التخريج، وهو نقل القول من مسألة إلى أخرى في ما إذا نص في حادثة على حكم ونص في مثلها على ضد ذلك الحكم ، فهذا النقل مشروط بعدم إمكان الفصل بين المسألتين، فلو أمكن الفصل لا يجمع بينهما بل يجب إبقاءهما على ظاهرهما . والنوع الثاني من التخريج مذكور قبل هذه المسألة. وحاصله : استخراج المسألة على وفق أصول الإمام بأن يجد دليلا من جنس ما يحتج به إمامه وعلى شرطه فیفتی بموجبه . وإذا وقع هذا النوع في صورة قد قال فيها بعض الأصحاب غير ذلك، سمّى "وجها"، كذا في فتاوى ابن الصلاح : ٣٤/١ ٣٥
Shaykh Abu 'Amr said: It is appropriate to base this on a disagreement reported by Shaykh Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi and others: that which our companions extrapolate, is it permissible to attribute it to al-Shafi'i? The soundest opinion is that it is not attributed to him. 32 - Then sometimes he extrapolates from a specific text of his Imam, and sometimes he does not find it, so he extrapolates based on his principles, by finding evidence on the condition of what his Imam uses as proof, and he gives fatwa accordingly. 33 - If his Imam has a text on something, and a text (2) on a similar matter that contradicts it, then he extrapolates from one to the other (3), it is called an "extrapolated opinion." ... (footnotes follow)... The condition of this extrapolation (1) is that he finds no distinction between the two texts; if he finds one, it is obligatory to keep both on their apparent meanings. They disagree greatly about the permissibility of extrapolation in such cases, due to their disagreement about the possibility of making a distinction. I say: Most of such cases can have a distinction, and they have mentioned it. They said: When Allah prescribed in the expiation for killing (the condition of) faith, and left it general in the expiation for zihar, we analogized one to the other and considered faith in both. Likewise here. Others said: It is not permissible, because he only stated a ruling in each of them, so one cannot attribute to him what he did not state. And apparently he intended a distinction between the two cases, so whoever combines them has contradicted him. The answer to their argument: There, a restriction is present in one place and omitted in the other, so we apply the unrestricted to the restricted, unlike our case where he stated in each of the two cases a ruling contrary to what he stated in the other, so analogy is not permissible with explicit contradiction. And the analogue of our case is the fasting in the expiation for tamattu' with the fasting in the expiation for killing and zihar; when he prescribed consecutiveness in zihar and killing, and prescribed separation in tamattu', it is not permissible to compare one to the other. But if he states a ruling in one case and a ruling in another that contradicts it, and it is impossible to separate the two cases, then there is no disagreement that his answer in one is transferred to the other, and they are taken as two opinions, and their ruling is like that of a single case in which two opinions were stated. And the correct is the second opinion, as stated in Sharh al-Luma'... (footnote: The condition of this extrapolation means the condition of the first type, which is transferring an opinion from one case to another when there is a text on an incident and a text on a similar incident with a contradictory ruling; this transfer is conditional on the impossibility of separating the two cases. If separation is possible, they are not combined but must remain on their apparent meanings. The second type of extrapolation is mentioned before this case, and its summary is: deriving a case according to the Imam's principles by finding evidence of the type the Imam uses and on his condition, and giving fatwa accordingly. If this type occurs in a form where some companions have said otherwise, it is called "wajh", as in Fatawa Ibn al-Salah: 1/34-35.)
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage from Imam al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa discusses the methodology of takhreej (extrapolation) in issuing fatwas. The author begins by stating a disagreement reported by al-Shirazi: whether rulings extrapolated by followers of Imam al-Shafi'i can be attributed to him. The sound opinion is that they are not absolutely attributed, but only with qualification (mukharraj). Two types of takhreej are distinguished: first, when the Imam has an explicit text on a similar case, and second, when no explicit text exists and the mufti derives a ruling from the Imam's principles (usul). The first type is called 'qawl mukharraj' (extrapolated opinion). The condition for this type is that no distinction (farq) exists between the two cases; if a distinction is possible, both rulings must be kept as they are. The scholars disagree on the permissibility of such cross-application, as exemplified by the case of kaffarat (expiation): Allah specified faith in the expiation for killing but left it general in zihar; analogizing one to another is accepted. However, when the Imam explicitly gives contradictory rulings in two cases that cannot be separated, the rulings are transferred to become two opinions in each case, effectively treating them as a single case with two rulings. The second type of takhreej, derived from the Imam's principles, is called 'wajh' if it contradicts some companions' views. From a Hanafi perspective, similar principles of takhreej exist, where later Hanafi scholars like al-Sarakhsi and al-Kasani derived rulings based on Abu Hanifa's usul, always ensuring the rulings align with the Imam's methodology.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhreej): Extrapolating a ruling for a new case based on the Imam's explicit texts on similar cases or on his established principles (usul).
قول مخرّج (qawl mukharraj): An opinion that is extracted (mukharraj) from the Imam's texts or principles, not directly stated by the Imam.
أصول (usul): The principles of jurisprudence and methodology used by the Imam (e.g., al-Shafi'i) to derive rulings.
وجه (wajh): A derived opinion based on the Imam's principles, especially when it contradicts some companions' views.
فرق (farq): A distinction or difference between two cases that prevents extrapolation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for transferring a ruling from one case to another in the first type of takhreej (when the Imam has texts on similar but contradictory cases)?
A) The mufti must be a mujtahid.
B) No distinction (farq) is found between the two cases.
C) The Imam must have explicitly allowed such transfer.
D) The two cases must be from the same chapter of fiqh.

Key Takeaway
Takhreej is a powerful tool for muftis to address new cases, but the mufti must clearly distinguish between the Imam's direct rulings and extrapolated ones.

The Condition for Takhreej When Texts Differ
Condition for transferring rulings between two contrasting texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for takhreej when two texts from the imam differ, and apply it to determine whether to keep them separate or treat them as a single case.

Core Idea
If you find a genuine difference between two texts, keep them separate—don't force an analogy.

This lesson addresses a foundational rasm al-mufti rule: what should a mufti do when he encounters two explicit statements from his imam that appear to prescribe different rulings for similar cases? The rule provides a clear condition that protects the integrity of the imam's words. Understanding this condition is essential to avoid arbitrary qiyas and to respect the imam's intended distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Identify Two Seemingly Conflicting Texts
Locate two explicit statements (nass) from your imam that appear to conflict. For example, one text may specify belief (iman) in an expiation while another leaves it unrestricted.
The texts must be directly from the imam, not from later jurists.
2
Search for a Genuine Difference
Examine the two cases thoroughly. Try to find any substantive difference (farq) between them—in their conditions, underlying causes, or textual wording.
The difference must be real and not merely apparent.
3
If a Difference Exists: Keep Separate
If you find a valid distinction, you must apply each text as it is (zahiruhuma). Do not combine them by analogy or transfer the ruling from one to the other.
Presuming that the imam intended each ruling for its specific case.
4
If No Difference Possible: Treat as One Case with Two Opinions
If, despite your best effort, no distinction can be made between the two cases, then they are essentially one case for which the imam gave two different opinions. You may then transfer one ruling to the other, and the case is treated as having two potential answers.
This is the only exception and is rarely invoked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط هذا التخريج (١) أن لا يجد بين نصيه فرقا، فإن وجده وجب تقريرهما على ظاهرهما . ويختلفون كثيراً في القول بالتخريج في مثل ذلك ؛ لاختلافهم في إمكان الفرق . قلت : وأكثر ذلك يمكن فيه الفرق وقد ذكروه . :وقالوا : إن الله تعالى لما نص فى كفارة القتل على الإيمان، وأطلق في كفارة الظهار قسنا إحداهما على الأخرى واعتبرنا الإيمان فيهما ، كذلك ههنا . وقال آخرون : لا يجوز؛ لأنه لم ينص في كل واحدة منهما إلا على قول، فلايجوز أن ينسب إليه ما لم ينص عليه . والآن الظاهر أنه قصد الفرق بين المسألتين، فمن جمع بينهما فقد خالفه . والجواب عن احتجاجهم : إن هناك قيد في إحدى الموضعين وأطلق في الآخر، فحملنا المطلق على المقيد ، بخلاف مسألتنا فإنه نص فى كل واحدة من المسألتين على حكم بخلاف ما نص على الأخرى، فلا يجوز القياس مع التصريح بالخلاف، وصار وزان مسألتنا الصوم في كفارة التمتع مع الصوم في كفارة القتل والظهار ؛ فإنه لما نص في الظهار والقتل على التتابع ونص فى التمتع على التفريق، لم يجز اعتبار أحدهما بالآخر، فأما إذا نص في مسألة على حكم ونص في غيرها على حكم يخالفه ولا يمكن الفصل بين المسألتين بوجه فلا خلاف أن جوابه في إحداهما ينقل إلى الأخرى، ويخرجان على قولين ويكون حكمهما حكم مسألة واحدة نص فيها على قولين . والصحيح هو القول الثاني كما صرح به في شرح اللمع : ص ١٠٨٣ ، والتبصرة، للشيخ الإمام أبي إسحاق إبراهيم بن على الشيرازي: ص٥١٦ . (١) قوله : " وشرط هذا التخريج " أى شرط النوع الأول من التخريج، وهو نقل القول من مسألة إلى أخرى في ما إذا نص في حادثة على حكم ونص في مثلها على ضد ذلك الحكم ، فهذا النقل مشروط بعدم إمكان الفصل بين المسألتين، فلو أمكن الفصل لا يجمع بينهما بل يجب إبقاءهما على ظاهرهما . والنوع الثاني من التخريج مذكور قبل هذه المسألة. وحاصله : استخراج المسألة على وفق أصول الإمام بأن يجد دليلا من جنس ما يحتج به إمامه وعلى شرطه فیفتی بموجبه . وإذا وقع هذا النوع في صورة قد قال فيها بعض الأصحاب غير ذلك، سمّى "وجها"، كذا في فتاوى ابن الصلاح : ٣٤/١ ٣٥
The condition of this takhreej is that he finds no difference between his two texts; if he finds a difference, it is obligatory to maintain them as they are. And they differ greatly regarding the use of takhreej in such a case, due to their difference regarding the possibility of a distinction. I say: Most of that can have a distinction, and they have mentioned it. And they said: Verily, Allah the Exalted, when He specified belief in the expiation for killing, and left it unrestricted in the expiation for zihar, we analogized one to the other and considered belief in both, likewise here. And others said: It is not permissible, because He did not specify in each of them except a ruling, so it is not permissible to attribute to Him what He did not specify. And now the apparent is that He intended a distinction between the two cases, so whoever combines them has contradicted Him. And the answer to their argument: There, a restriction is in one of the two places and unrestricted in the other, so we carry the unrestricted to the restricted, unlike our case, for He specified in each of the two cases a ruling contrary to what He specified in the other, so analogy is not permissible with explicit contradiction, and the measure of our case is the fast in the expiation for tamattu' with the fast in the expiation for killing and zihar; for when He specified sequentiality in zihar and killing and specified separation in tamattu', it was not permissible to analogize one to the other. But if He specifies a ruling in one case and specifies in another a ruling that contradicts it and it is impossible to separate the two cases in any way, then there is no disagreement that his answer in one of them is transferred to the other, and they are derived as two opinions, and their ruling is the ruling of a single case in which two opinions are specified. And the correct is the second opinion, as explained in Sharh al-Luma' p. 1083, and al-Tabsirah by Shaykh Imam Abu Ishaq Ibrahim bin Ali al-Shirazi p. 516. (1) His statement: 'And the condition of this takhreej' means the condition of the first type of takhreej, which is transferring a statement from one case to another when a ruling is specified in an incident and a ruling contrary to that is specified in a similar incident; this transfer is conditional upon the impossibility of distinguishing between the two cases. If distinction is possible, they are not combined but must be kept as they are. The second type of takhreej is mentioned before this issue. Its summary is: deriving a case according to the principles of the imam by finding evidence of the type used by his imam and on his condition, and then issuing a fatwa accordingly. If this type occurs in a scenario where some of the companions have said otherwise, it is called 'wajh'. This is as in Fatawa Ibn al-Salah: 1/34-35.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage, from Imam al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa, establishes a key rasm rule for takhreej (deriving rulings by analogy from the imam's texts). The condition: when you find two texts from the imam that seem to conflict, you must first check if there is a genuine difference (farq) between them. If there is, each text is applied as is, and you cannot combine them by analogy. The text then presents a classical dispute: one group allows qiyas when one text is restricted and the other absolute, but the correct view (al-qawl al-thani) is that if the imam explicitly prescribes different rulings, qiyas is barred. The only exception is when the two cases are truly inseparable, in which case they are treated as one case with two opinions. The footnote clarifies that this is the first type of takhreej; the second type involves deriving new rulings based on the imam's principles and evidence. This rule prevents arbitrary conflation of distinct rulings and preserves the authority of the imam's explicit statements.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhreej): Deriving a ruling for a new case by transferring a statement from a similar case from the imam's texts, or by extracting it according to the imam's principles.
نص (nass): An explicit textual statement from the imam (here, from the sources, but in context of the imam of the madhhab) prescribing a ruling.
فرق (farq): A genuine difference or distinction between two cases that justifies treating them separately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the mufta bihi (correct) view when two texts from the imam differ?
A) Always combine them by analogy to maintain consistency.
B) Treat each text as it is if a difference exists; otherwise, treat as one case with two opinions.
C) Ignore the older text and follow the newer one.
D) Refer the matter to a consensus of the companions.

Key Takeaway
When two texts from the imam differ, the default is to keep them separate; only when absolutely no distinction can be found do they merge into a single case with two opinions.

Conditions for Muftis and the Ruling on a Muqallid Giving Fatwa
Explains conditions for muftis and limits of muqallid fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two essential qualities of a mufti in the Hanafi school and apply the rule that a muqallid must attribute his fatwa to the madhhab.

Core Idea
A mufti must have both hifdh al-madhhab and fiqh al-nafs; a muqallid may only transmit, not independently judge.

This passage from Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti lays down the foundational conditions for anyone who dares to issue fatwa. It warns that even a skilled usuli without a madhhab is not qualified, and it carefully defines the limited role of a mere transmitter. Understanding these boundaries is essential for anyone who intends to practice iftaa within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Recognise the two fundamental conditions for a mufti
The passage states that every category of mufti requires hifdh al-madhhab (preserving the madhhab) and fiqh al-nafs (deep understanding). These are non-negotiable.
Fiqh al-nafs goes beyond memorisation; it is an intuitive grasp of rulings.
2
Understand the prohibition for non-qualified persons
Even a proficient usuli or debater who has not preserved a specific madhhab cannot give fatwa independently. He must consult or ask.
Imam al-Haramayn is cited as authority for this strict rule.
3
Analyse the role of the qasir (deficient transmitter)
A person who has memorised books but lacks deep understanding may only transmit exact rulings from reliable texts. He must not analogise, even if he thinks the analogy is correct.
This is the limit of taqlid – transmission, not ijtihad.
4
Evaluate the dispute on a muqallid giving fatwa
Al-Halimi, al-Juwayni, and others forbid it absolutely; al-Qaffal permits it. Abu Amr clarifies that the forbidding view means the muqallid must attribute the ruling to his imam.
The Hanafi relied-upon position requires attribution.
5
Apply the rule: requirement of attribution
In practice, muqallid muftis are not muftis in reality but stand in for them. They must say 'the madhhab of so-and-so is such.' Omitting attribution is only allowed if context makes it obvious.
This protects the questioner from confusion about authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في بيان ما يشترط لهذه الأقسام
٤١ - هذه أصناف المفتين وهى خمسة وكل صنف منها يشترط فيه حفظ المذهب، وفقه النفس . فمن تصدى للفتيا، وليس بهذه الصفة، فقد باء بأمر عظيم
٤٢ - ولقد قطع إمام الحرمين وغيره بأن الأصولي الماهر المتصرف في الفقه لا يحل له الفتوى بمجرد ذلك . ولو وقعت له واقعة لزمه أن يسأل عنها . ويلتحق به المتصرف النظار البحاث من أئمة الخلاف، وفحول المناظرين؛ لأنه ليس أهلا لإدراك حكم الواقعة استقلالا ؛ لقصور آلته، ولا (٢) من مذهب ولا(٢) إمام ؛ لعدم حفظه له على الوجه المعتبر ٤٣ - فإن قيل : من حفظ كتاباً أو أكثر في المذهب وهو قاصر لم يتصف بصفة أحد ممن سبق، ولم يجد العامي في بلده غيره، هل له الرجوع إلى قوله؟ فالجواب : إن كان في غير بلده مفت يجد السبيل إليه، وجب التوصل إليه بحسب إمكانه . فإن تعذر ذكر مسألته للقاصر. فإن وجدها بعينها في کتاب موثوق بصحته وهو ممن يقبل خبره ، نقل له حكمها بنصه، وكان العامى فيها مقلّداً صاحب المذهب. قال أبو عمرو : وهذا وجدته في ضمن كلام بعضهم، والدليل يعضده. وإن لم يجدها مسطورة بعينها لم يقسها على مسطور عنده، وإن اعتقده من قياس لا فارق ؛ فإنه قد يتوهم ذلك في غير موضعه . ٤٤ - فإن قيل : هل لمقلّد أن يفتى بما هو مقلّد فيه؟ قلنا : قطع أبو عبد الله الحليمى، وأبو محمد الجويني، وأبو المحاسن الرؤياني، وغيرهم بتحريمه وقال القفال المروزي : يجوز . قال أبو عمرو : قول من منعه معناه : لا يذكره على صورة من يقوله من عند نفسه بل يضيفه إلى إمامه الذي قلده . ٤٥ - فعلى هذا من عددناه من المفتين المقلدين ليسوا مفتين حقيقة، لكن لما قاموا مقامهم، وأدوا عنهم، عُدوا معهم. وسبيلهم أن يقولوا مثلا : مذهب الشافعي كذا ، أو نحو هذا. ومن ترك منهم الإضافة فهو اكتفاء بالمعلوم من الحال عن التصريح به، ولا بأس بذلك . ٤٦ - وذكر صاحب "الحاوي " في العامي إذا عرف حكم حادثة بناء على دليلها ثلاثة أوجه : أحدها: يجوز أن يفتى به (٢) ، ويجوز تقليده ؛ لأنه وصل إلى علمه
Section: On explaining what is required for these categories. 41 - These are the categories of muftis, and they are five. Each category requires preservation of the madhhab and understanding of the subject matter. Whoever undertakes giving fatwa without possessing these attributes has indeed committed a grave matter. 42 - Imam al-Haramayn and others decisively ruled that a proficient usuli who is capable in fiqh is not permitted to give fatwa based solely on that. And if a case occurs for him, he must ask about it. This also applies to the proficient debater and researcher from the imams of ikhtilaf and the leading debaters; because he is not qualified to independently comprehend the ruling of an incident due to deficiency in his tools, and [he] has neither a madhhab nor an imam due to not preserving it in the required manner. 43 - If it is said: Someone who has memorized a book or more in the madhhab, though he is deficient and does not possess the attributes of any of those mentioned previously, and a layperson in his town finds no one else, can the layperson refer to his statement? The answer: If there is a mufti in another town that he can reach, he must endeavor to reach him to the extent possible. If that is not possible, he presents his issue to the deficient one. If he finds the exact ruling in a trustworthy book, and he is one whose report is accepted, he transmits the ruling verbatim from it, and the layperson is in that case a muqallid of the founder of the madhhab. Abu Amr said: This I found within the words of some of them, and the evidence supports it. If he does not find it written verbatim, he should not analogize it to something written using his own analogy, even if he believes it is a correct analogy with no difference; because he might be mistaken in that. 44 - If it is said: Can a muqallid give fatwa on what he is a muqallid in? We say: Abu Abdullah al-Halimi, Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni, Abu al-Mahasin al-Ruwayani, and others decisively ruled it is forbidden. Al-Qaffal al-Marwazi said it is permissible. Abu Amr said: The meaning of the one who forbids it is that he should not mention it as if speaking from himself, but rather attribute it to his imam whom he follows. 45 - Therefore, those we counted among the muqallid muftis are not muftis in reality, but because they stand in their place and convey from them, they are counted with them. Their method should be to say, for example, 'the madhhab of al-Shafi'i is such' or similar. If any of them omits the attribution, it is because the context makes it known, and there is no harm in that. 46 - The author of al-Hawi mentioned regarding the layperson if he knows the ruling of an incident based on its evidence: three opinions: one of them: he may give fatwa with it, and his taqlid is permissible, because he has attained knowledge of it.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage from Imam Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa outlines the conditions for becoming a mufti and addresses the status of those who merely transmit the madhhab. The passage begins by stating there are five categories of muftis (elsewhere defined as mujtahid mutlaq, mujtahid fi al-madhhab, etc.), each requiring hifdh al-madhhab (memorization of the madhhab) and fiqh al-nafs (deep understanding of the subject). Without these, one commits a grave sin by giving fatwa. Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) emphasizes that even a skilled usuli who has not preserved a specific madhhab cannot give fatwa independently; he must consult others. This applies to those who are masters of legal theory and debate but do not adhere to a single madhhab—they are not qualified to derive rulings independently due to insufficient tools. The passage then addresses a practical scenario: a layperson in a town with no qualified mufti but only a person who has memorized a book(s) of the madhhab without deep understanding. The solution is to seek a real mufti elsewhere if possible. If not, the layperson may present his issue to this 'qasir' (deficient person). If the qasir finds the exact ruling in a reliable book and is trustworthy, he may transmit it verbatim, and the layperson becomes a muqallid of the madhhab's imam. However, the qasir must not analogize from that text, even if he thinks the analogy is sound, as he may err. This shows the strict prohibition of ijtihad for non-mujtahids. The next section (44) deals with a muqallid (one who follows an imam without direct evidence) giving fatwa on what he follows. Most scholars (including al-Halimi, al-Juwayni, al-Ruwayani) forbid it absolutely, while al-Qaffal permits it. Abu Amr clarifies the forbidding view means the muqallid must attribute the ruling to his imam, not speak as if it is his own. In practice, muqallid muftis are not true muftis but stand in for them; they should say 'the madhhab of so-and-so is such.' Omitting attribution is acceptable if the context makes it clear. Finally, the author of al-Hawi (al-Mawardi) reports three opinions on a layperson who knows a ruling from its evidence: one allows him to give fatwa and be followed, as he has attained certain knowledge. This passage is directly relevant to Hanafi usul al-iftaa. In the Hanafi school, the conditions for mufti are similarly strict: a mufti must be a mujtahid at least within the madhhab (mujtahid fi al-madhhab). The Hanafi position on a muqallid giving fatwa is that he may not issue independent rulings; he must attribute them to the authoritative texts or to the imams of the madhhab. However, the later Hanafi tradition recognized 'mufti of the madhhab' who, while not absolute mujtahids, are qualified to issue fatwa based on the relied-upon positions (zahir al-riwayah) due to their thorough knowledge of the madhhab's texts and methodology. This aligns with the compromise mentioned here: they are muftis by representation. The dispute between al-Halimi and al-Qaffal mirrors Hanafi internal discussions about whether a mere transmitter can be called a mufti. The Hanafi resolution is that he may give fatwa but must clearly indicate the source, as stated in Rasm al-Mufti.

Key Terms
الحفظ (al-hifdh): Memorization and comprehensive knowledge of the inherited rulings of the madhhab and its sources.
فقه النفس (fiqh al-nafs): Deep, innate understanding and insight into the subject matter, enabling correct application.
قاصر (qasir): A person deficient in knowledge or qualifications for independent ijtihad; one who has memorized texts but lacks deep understanding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about a person who has memorized a book but lacks deep understanding (qasir) when asked a question?
A) He may give fatwa independently.
B) He may transmit exact texts only.
C) He may analogize based on what he has memorized.
D) He cannot give any fatwa.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must possess both knowledge of the madhhab and deep understanding; a muqallid mufti must always attribute rulings to the madhhab, never to himself.

Ruling of Ifta' being Fard Kifaya and When It Becomes Fard 'Ayn
Ruling on the obligation of ifta' and its individualization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the obligation of ifta' (fard kifaya) and identify the conditions under which it becomes fard 'ayn, applying the Hanafi rasm al-mufti.

Core Idea
Ifta' is a collective duty; it becomes individual only when no other qualified mufti exists and harm is feared.

This passage establishes the foundational ruling on the obligation of issuing fatwas. It clarifies that while ifta' is generally a collective duty, it can become individually obligatory upon a mufti when certain conditions are met. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the general case and the exceptional case, ensuring that religious obligations are fulfilled without undue burden. Understanding this ruling is essential for any student of ifta'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The passage begins by stating that ifta' is fard kifaya. Understand that this means if some qualified muftis answer, the sin falls from the rest. Note the collective nature of the duty.
2
Identify the exception for individual obligation
When a mufti is the only qualified person in the area, issuing a fatwa becomes fard 'ayn upon him. This is the first condition for individualization.
This is the basic trigger.
3
Examine the scenario with another mufti absent
If another mufti exists but is not present, there are two views: the soundest (as per the author) is that it does not become fard 'ayn; the second view analogizes to testimony. Understand the difference.
The soundest view is preferred.
4
Reconcile the views with the harm condition
The commentary reconciles: if not answering would cause harm to the questioner (e.g., missing a wajib or falling into haram), then it becomes fard 'ayn. Otherwise, it remains collective.
This is the key nuance.
5
Apply the hadith on concealing knowledge
The hadith about concealing knowledge is not absolute; it applies only when teaching is individually obligatory. Recognize that the hadith is restricted to cases like explaining Islam to a new Muslim or teaching prayer.
Do not generalize the hadith to all questions.

كفاية (٣) . وإن لم يحضر غيره فوجهان : أصحهما لا يتعين (4)؛ لما سبق عن ابن
أبي ليلى (١). والثاني : يتعين وهما كالوجهين فى مثله في الشهادة (٢).

(٣) قوله : " فرض كفاية " في البحر عن الروض : " فإن لم يكن غيره تعين عليه، وإن كان غيره فهو فرض كفاية، ومع هذا لا يحل التسارع إلى ما لا يتحقق " .

Chapter on the rulings of muftis, containing issues. First: 47 - Issuing fatwa is a collective duty (fard kifaya). If someone seeks a fatwa and there is no one else in that area, it becomes individually obligatory upon him to answer. If there is someone else and they are present, then answering is a collective duty for both. If the other is not present, then there are two views: the sounder is that it does not become individually obligatory, due to what was previously mentioned from Ibn Abi Layla. The second view is that it becomes individually obligatory, and these two views are like the two views in the analogous case of testimony.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the obligation of issuing fatwas. It states that ifta' is a collective duty (fard kifaya), meaning if some qualified muftis answer, the obligation is fulfilled for all. However, if a mufti is the only one in the area, it becomes individually obligatory (fard 'ayn) upon him to answer. The text then discusses a scenario where there is another mufti but he is not present. There are two opinions: the sounder (as stated by the author) is that it does not become individually obligatory because the other mufti could potentially fulfill the duty. The second opinion, analogized to testimony, holds that being asked makes it obligatory. The commentary reconciles these views: if the absence of the other mufti leads to harm (e.g., the questioner missing a religious obligation or falling into sin), then answering becomes individually obligatory; otherwise, it does not. The passage also addresses the hadith about concealing knowledge, explaining that it applies specifically to cases where teaching is individually obligatory, such as explaining Islam to a new Muslim or teaching prayer.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifaya): A collective obligation; if performed by some, the sin falls from the rest.
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An individual obligation incumbent upon every qualified person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does ifta' become an individual obligation (fard 'ayn) according to the soundest view in this passage?
A) Whenever a mufti is asked a question.
B) Only when there is no other mufti in the area and harm is feared from not answering.
C) Always, because knowledge must be conveyed.
D) Only when the question is about halal and haram.

Key Takeaway
Ifta' is a collective duty that becomes individually obligatory only when the mufti is the sole qualified person and harm would result from not answering.

Answering Hypothetical Questions: Ruling for Mufti
Ruling on answering questions about events not yet occurred

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a Hanafi mufti is obligated, recommended, or discouraged from answering a hypothetical question about an event not yet occurred.

Core Idea
A mufti is not obligated to answer hypotheticals unless harm would result from silence, adjusting the ruling based on consequence.

When a seeker asks about a scenario that hasn't happened, should a mufti answer? This passage from Rasm al-Mufti provides a nuanced rule: while the default is non-obligation, the mufti must assess potential harm and benefit, leading to a graded response. The ruling balances textual authority and practical consequence, reflecting a uniquely Hanafi consideration of maqasid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core default ruling
Locate the initial statement: 'he should not answer' regarding hypotheticals. This sets the default position that answering is not generally required.
The default is non-obligation, but it is not absolute.
2
Parse the two conflicting positions
The text presents two opinions: one says answering is not incumbent (because others can take his place), another says it is incumbent (because being asked creates an obligation to inform of Allah's ruling). Understand the dalil for each.
These positions mirror a classical debate on the obligation of a witness when called.
3
Extract the reconciliation (taṭbīq)
The passage provides a specific reconciliation: if there is no other mufti in town and harm would befall the asker (missing a wajib or falling into haram), then answering becomes obligatory; otherwise not.
This conditional obligation is the operative Hanafi position.
4
Analyze the detailed preference from Ibn al-Qayyim
Ibn al-Qayyim outlines three opinions among the Salaf and concludes with a detailed taxonomy: if a clear text exists, answering is not disliked; if no text and the event is far-fetched, it is not recommended; if the event is plausible and the seeker aims for fahm and taṣawwur, answering is recommended.
This nuanced approach aligns with Hanafi reliance on maṣlaḥa and darar.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a specific hypothetical, determine the mufti's ruling based on the existence of a text, the likelihood of the event, and the presence of other scholars. Practice balancing the factors.
The final ruling depends on contextual conditions, not a blanket rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤٨ - ولو سأل عامى عما لم يقع ، لم يجب جوابه (۳) مستفتيّا في حلال وحرام ؛ فإنه يلزم في هذه الأمور أن لا يمتنع من الجواب، ويرشده إلى الصواب، ومن لم يفعل ذلك كان آثما مستحقاً للوعيد، وليس الأمر كذلك في ما سواه. (٤) قوله : "أصحهما لا يتعين" لأن غيره يقوم مقامه، فلم يتعين عليه الجواب، ووجه القول الآخر أنه لما سئل فقد تعين عليه الإخبار بحكم الله ورسوله، والتطبيق بين القولين : أنه إذا لم يوجد في تلك القرية غيره وخيف من امتناعه عن الجواب أن يلحق الضرر بالسائل بأن يفوت عنه واجب شرعى أو يقع في الحرام ونحو ذلك، تعين عليه، وإلا لا . (۳) قوله : "لم يجب جوابه قال ابن القيم رحمه الله تعالى : إذا سأل المستفتي عن مسألة لم تقع، فهل تستحب أجابته أو تكره أو تخير؟ فيه ثلاثة أقوال، وقد حكى عن كثير من السلف أنه كان لا يتكلم فيما لم يقع ، وكان بعض السلف إذا سأله الرجل عن مسألة ، قال : " هل كان ذلك؟ " فإن قال : نعم تكلف له الجواب، وإلا قال : دعنا في عافية". وقال الإمام أحمد لبعض أصحابه: "إياك أن تتكلم في مسألة . ليس لك فيها إمام. والحق التفصيل، فإن كان في المسألة نص عن كتاب الله أو سنة عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أو أثر عن الصحابة لم يكره الكلام فيها، وإذا لم يكن فيها نص ولا أثر ، فإن كانت بعيدة الوقوع أو مقدرة لا تقع، لم يستحب له الكلام فيها، وإن كان وقوعها غير نادر ولا مستبعد وغرض السائل الإحاطة بعلمها؛ ليكون منها على بصيرة إذا وقعت استحب له الجواب بما يعلم، لا سيما إن كان السائل يتفقه بذلك ويعتبر بها نظائرها ، ويفرع عليها، فحيث كانت مصلحة الجواب راجحة كان هو الأولى.
48 - And if a commoner asks about something that has not occurred, he should not answer him (3) seeking a fatwa in halal and haram; for it is necessary in these matters that he does not refrain from answering, and guides him to correctness, and whoever does not do that is sinful deserving of threat, and the matter is not so in other than that. (4) His statement: "The sounder opinion is that it is not incumbent" because someone else can take his place, so answering is not incumbent upon him. The basis of the other opinion is that since he was asked, he is obligated to inform of the ruling of Allah and His Messenger. The reconciliation between the two views: if there is no one else in that town and it is feared that if he refrains from answering, harm will befall the asker such that a religious obligation will be missed or he will fall into the forbidden and the like, then it becomes incumbent; otherwise not. (1) His statement: "Due to what preceded from Ibn Abi Layla" which is what was narrated from him that he said: "I met one hundred and twenty of the Ansar from the Companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). One of them would be asked about a matter and he would pass it on, this one to that one, and that one to this one, until it returned to the first." In another narration: "None of them would narrate a hadith but that he wished his brother would suffice him of it, and none would be asked for a fatwa but that he wished his brother would suffice him of the fatwa." (2) His statement: "Concerning testimony" - when a witness is summoned to testify, is it obligatory to perform the testimony? There are two views. One: obligation, because he has been specified by the summoning, and because he is prohibited from withholding by His statement: "And let not the witnesses refuse when they are called." Second: no obligation, because someone else can take his place, so it is as if he was not summoned. (3) His statement: "He should not answer" - Ibn al-Qayyim (may Allah have mercy on him) said: If the seeker asks about a matter that has not occurred, is it recommended to answer, or disliked, or is there a choice? There are three opinions. It is reported from many of the Salaf that they would not speak about what has not occurred. Some of the Salaf, when a man asked about a matter, would say: "Has that happened?" If he said yes, he would undertake to answer; otherwise he would say: "Leave us in safety." Imam Ahmad said to some of his companions: "Beware of speaking on a matter for which you have no imam." The truth is detail: if there is a text from the Book of Allah, a Sunnah from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), or an athar from the Companions, then speaking about it is not disliked. If there is no text or athar, then if its occurrence is far-fetched or hypothetical and not likely to occur, it is not recommended to speak about it. If its occurrence is not rare or improbable, and the asker's purpose is to encompass knowledge of it so that he may be upon insight when it occurs, then it is recommended for him to answer with what he knows, especially if the asker seeks to gain fiqh from it, derive analogies, and branch out rulings. Wherever the benefit of answering is preponderant, it is preferable.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage addresses a rasm rule for muftis: answering hypothetical questions about events that have not occurred. The core ruling presented is that a mufti is generally not obligated to answer such questions, but there is a significant detail. The commentary reconciles two positions: the first (sounder) opinion says it is not incumbent because another mufti can be found, while the second says it becomes incumbent because the question specifically targets him. The resolution: if no other qualified mufti exists in the locality and harm (e.g., missing an obligation or falling into sin) is feared, then answering becomes obligatory; otherwise not. The passage then provides background from Ibn Abi Layla about the practice of early Companions who refrained from giving fatwas whenever possible. It also draws a parallel with the obligation of a summoned witness, where there is a similar ikhtilaf. Finally, it quotes Ibn al-Qayyim detailing three scholarly opinions on answering hypotheticals and concludes with a detailed preference: if there is a clear text (Qur'an, Sunnah, or Companion athar), it is not disliked; if no text, and the event is far-fetched, it is not recommended; but if the event is plausible and the seeker wants to be prepared, then answering is recommended, especially if there is a clear benefit. This reflects the Hanafi approach that considers the maqasid (objectives) of the Shariah.

Key Terms
ما لم يقع (mā lam yaqa'): An event that has not yet occurred; a hypothetical scenario presented in a question to the mufti.
مستفتي (mustaftī): A person seeking a fatwa, regardless of whether the event has occurred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciling position in this passage, when does answering a hypothetical question become incumbent upon the mufti?
A) Whenever the question is about halal and haram.
B) When no other mufti exists in the town and harm is feared from withholding the answer.
C) Only if the event has already occurred.
D) Always, because the mufti is obligated to spread knowledge.

Key Takeaway
A mufti's duty to answer hypotheticals is conditional: obligated only when harm is feared, recommended when benefit preponderates, and avoided when the scenario is far-fetched.
