Retraction of a Fatwa: Effect on the Seeker
Ruling on validity of fatwa after mufti retracts it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-ijtihad la yunqadu bil-ijtihad' to determine the validity of past actions after a mufti's retraction.

Core Idea
Past actions based on valid ijtihad are not undone by a later retraction.

When a mufti retracts a fatwa, the effect on the seeker depends on timing and the nature of the original fatwa. The Hanafi school upholds the maxim 'ijtihad does not nullify ijtihad,' preserving past actions based on valid ijtihad. This lesson unpacks the detailed ruling as conveyed by Hanafi masters like al-Saymari and al-Khatib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the timing of the seeker's action relative to retraction
Determine whether the seeker acted before or after the mufti's retraction. If before, the original fatwa may still have effect; if after, it cannot be used.
2
Assess the nature of the original fatwa
Was the original fatwa based on ijtihad in a matter open to interpretation, or did it contradict definitive evidence (qat'i)? This determines whether the past action can stand.
3
Apply the corresponding rule
If the action was before retraction and the fatwa was ijtihadi, the action stands. If it contradicted qat'i evidence, it must be undone. If the action was after retraction, it cannot be based on the retracted fatwa.
4
Test with the marriage example
If the seeker married based on the fatwa and continued, retraction necessitates separation because the marriage is ongoing and the basis is invalidated. This matches the analogy of changing qibla during prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثانية : ٤١ ٤٩ - إذا أفتى بشيء ثم رجع عنه، فإن علم المستفتى برجوعه، ولم يكن عمل بالأول، لم يجز العمل به ) ، وكذا إن نكح بفتواه واستمر على نكاح ،فتواه ثم رجع لزمه مفارقتها، كما نر تغير اجتهاد من قلده في القبلة في أثناء صلاته . وإن كان عمل قبل رجوعه، فإن خالف دليلا قاطعاً، لزم المستفتى نقض عمله ذلك . وإن كان في محل اجتهاد لم يلزمه نقضه ؛ لأن الاجتهاد لا ينقض بالاجتهاد (۳). وهذا التفصيل ذكره الصيمرى والخطيب وأبو عمرو، واتفقوا (۲) قوله : " لأن الاجتهاد لا ينقض بالاجتهاد" فإذا كان المجتهد حاكماً وقضى في مسألة بحكم معين حسب اجتهاده، لا يجوز لحاكم آخر نقض هذا الاجتهاد، ولكن لو عرضت مسألة أخرى مثل الأول على الحاكم نفسه، وبدا له رأى جديد في هذه المسألة، فإن عليه أن يحكم باجتهاده الجديد، أما ما حكم به أولا فلا ينتقض بل يمضى، ومعنى هذا أن السوابق القضائية لا تقيد القاضى المسلم، وعلى هذا دل عمل القضاة في الإسلام من ذلك أن عمر بن الخطاب رضى الله عنه قضى في المسألة الحجرية في الميراث بعدم توريث أولاد الأبوين، ثم عرضت له نفس المسألة من بعده فقضى بتوريث أولاد الأبوين مع الأولاد لأ، فاعترض عليه أصحاب القضية الأولى، فقال: "ذلك ما قضينا وهذا على ما نقضى" .
Second: 41 49 - If he gave a fatwa on something and then retracted it, then if the seeker knows of his retraction and had not acted upon the first, it is not permissible to act upon it. Likewise, if he married based on his fatwa and continued in the marriage, then the mufti retracted, he must separate from her, just as we see the change of ijtihad of one who followed him in the qibla during his prayer. And if he acted before his retraction: if it contradicts definitive evidence, the seeker must undo his action; but if it is in a matter of ijtihad, he is not required to undo it, because ijtihad does not nullify ijtihad (3). This detail was mentioned by al-Saymari, al-Khatib, and Abu 'Amr, and they agreed. (2) His statement: "Because ijtihad does not nullify ijtihad" - if a mujtahid is a judge and ruled in a case with a specific ruling according to his ijtihad, it is not permissible for another judge to nullify this ijtihad. However, if another similar case is presented to the same judge and he forms a new opinion on this matter, he must rule according to his new ijtihad. As for what he ruled first, it is not nullified but stands. This means that judicial precedents do not bind the Muslim judge. The practice of judges in Islam indicates this, including that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) ruled in the case of al-mas'ala al-hajariyya in inheritance by not giving inheritance to the siblings through the mother, then the same case was presented to him later and he ruled to give inheritance to the siblings through the mother together with the children. The people of the first case objected, and he said: "That is what we ruled then, and this is what we rule now."
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage discusses a rasm rule for muftis: the effect of a mufti's retraction of his fatwa. The ruling is detailed according to two scenarios. First, if the seeker knows of the retraction and has not yet acted, he cannot act upon the original fatwa. Second, if he has acted (e.g., by marrying based on the fatwa and the marriage continued), and the mufti retracts, the seeker must separate from his wife, similar to changing ijtihad in the direction of qibla during prayer. If the action was performed before the retraction, the key distinction is whether the original fatwa opposed definitive evidence (such as a clear text) or was in a realm of ijtihad. In the first case, the seeker must undo his action; in the second, he is not required to undo it, based on the principle that 'ijtihad does not nullify ijtihad.' The commentary then explains this principle: a judge's previous decision cannot be overturned by another judge's differing ijtihad, but the same judge may adopt a new ijtihad for future cases. The example of 'Umar's change in the inheritance ruling is cited. This reflects the Hanafi view that ijtihad-based rulings are valid for their time and situation, but new ijtihad can supersede for future instances.

Key Terms
رجوع (rujū'): The mufti's withdrawal or reversal of his previous fatwa.
الاجتهاد لا ينقض بالاجتهاد (al-ijtihād lā yunqaḍu bil-ijtihād): A legal maxim meaning that a ruling based on ijtihad cannot be overturned by another ijtihad, except in certain cases of definitive evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a mufti retracts a fatwa after the seeker has already married based on that fatwa, what must the seeker do?
A) He must divorce his wife immediately.
B) He must undo the marriage only if the retraction was due to a change in ijtihad.
C) He must separate from his wife regardless of the reason for retraction.
D) He may continue the marriage because he acted before the retraction.

Key Takeaway
The effect of a mufti's retraction depends on whether the seeker acted before or after, and whether the fatwa contradicted definitive evidence; past ijtihadi actions are preserved.

Revoking a Fatwa That Contradicts the Imam's Nass
Ruling on mufti retracting fatwa upon discovering contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a muqallid mufti must revoke a fatwa when he becomes certain it contradicts his imam's explicit text, even in ijtihad matters.

Core Idea
When a mufti's fatwa certainly contradicts his imam's text, he must revoke it — even in ijtihad matters.

A mufti who follows Imam Abu Hanifa's madhhab may sometimes realize that a fatwa he issued goes against a clear text (nass) of the imam. This lesson explains the obligation to retract such a fatwa, grounded in the authority of the imam's text for the muqallid mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mufti's role
The mufti in this rule is a muqallid who issues fatwa according to a specific imam's madhhab. He is not an independent mujtahid.
This distinction is crucial for understanding why the imam's text is binding.
2
Determine the condition for revocation
The mufti must be certain (qati') that his fatwa contradicts the explicit text of his imam. Mere doubt or preference is insufficient.
Certainty here means there is no room for alternative interpretation within the madhhab.
3
Apply the rule even in ijtihad matters
Even if the original fatwa was in an area permissible for ijtihad (where multiple valid opinions exist), once the contradiction with the imam's text is confirmed, revocation is wajib.
This prevents the mufti from using ijtihad as a shield.
4
Understand the rationale
For the muqallid, the imam's text holds the same authority as a revealed text (nass al-shari') for an independent mujtahid. Therefore, contradicting it makes the fatwa void.
This analogy highlights the binding nature of the madhhab's primary sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٥٠ - قال أبو عمرو : وإذا كان يفتى على مذهب إمام، فرجع لكونه بان له قطعا مخالفة نص مذهب إمامه، وجب نقضه، وإن كان في محل الاجتهاد ؛ لأن نص مذهب إمامه في حقه كنص الشارع في حق المجتهد المستقل.
50. Abu Amr said: If a person gives fatwa according to the madhhab of an imam, then he retracts because it became clear to him with certainty that his fatwa contradicts the text of his imam's madhhab, then he must revoke it, even if it is in a matter of ijtihad; because the text of his imam's madhhab is for him like the text of the Lawgiver for the independent mujtahid.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental rule of mufti ethics: when a muqallid mufti (who follows a specific imam's madhhab) issues a fatwa, and subsequently realizes with certainty that the fatwa contradicts the explicit text (nass) of his imam's madhhab, he is obligated to revoke that fatwa. The ruling applies even if the original fatwa was in a matter open to ijtihad within the madhhab. The reason given is that for a muqallid mufti, the explicit text of his imam carries the same authority as a revealed text carries for an independent mujtahid. Therefore, any fatwa that contradicts that text is void and must be withdrawn. This is a rafi' (invalidation) of the earlier fatwa, not merely a preference. The mufti must inform the mustafti of the error and correct it.

Key Terms
نقض (naqd): Revocation or invalidation of a previous fatwa when it is found to be erroneous
مذهب إمام (madhhab al-imam): The specific legal school of a mujtahid imam (e.g., Abu Hanifa) to which the mufti adheres
مجتهد مستقل (mujtahid mustaqill): An independent mujtahid who derives rulings directly from Quran and Sunnah
قطعي (qat'i): Certain; the mufti must be absolutely sure of the contradiction

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When he learns of a more preferable opinion from another imam
B) When he realizes with certainty that his fatwa contradicts the explicit text of his imam's madhhab
C) Only when the mustafti complains about the fatwa
D) When the fatwa was given in matters of worship only

Key Takeaway
A muqallid mufti must revoke a fatwa if he becomes certain that it contradicts the explicit text of his imam, because that text holds the same authority as revelation for an independent mujtahid.

Conditions for Relying on Books in Fatwa
Ruling on mufti's reliance on trustworthy and well-known books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi conditions for relying on a book in fatwa, distinguish between well-known and obscure sources, and evaluate the permissibility of using unreliable copies.

Core Idea
A mufti should only rely on well-known books; but a qualified mufti may use an unreliable copy if it aligns with madhhab principles.

When a mufti issues a fatwa, he must ensure his sources are authentic. This lesson from al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa, expanded by later scholars, establishes a hierarchy: most reliable are well-known books like al-Hidayah; then books with valid isnad; then, with caution, unreliable copies if the mufti is competent. This protects the religion while allowing practical flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline rule
Imam al-Nawawi states that the mufti should only rely on a book whose authenticity is trusted and that represents the madhhab of the imam. This is the starting point.
2
Understand the epistemic justification
Al-Qari and al-Qarafi provide the rationale: well-known books are safe from distortion, while obscure ones are dangerous. The original strict principle required formal narration, but later scholars accepted fame as a safeguard.
3
Apply the hierarchy
For a reliable copy, rely fully. For an unreliable copy, verify with other copies or use only if the mufti is competent to derive and the ruling aligns with madhhab principles.
This is based on Abu 'Amr's ruling.
4
Note the adab of transmission
When citing from an unreliable copy, the mufti should use cautious language like 'I found' or 'it reached me', not attribute directly.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Ibn 'Abidin and later scholars hold that tawatur (widespread transmission) is not necessary; ghalabat al-zann (high probability) suffices, supported by the practice of scholars and judges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى يعتمد إلا على كتاب موثوق بصحته، وبأنه مذهب ذلك الإمام (١). فإن وثق بأن أصل التصنيف بهذه الصفة، لكن لم تكن هذه النسخة معتمدة، فليستظهر (٢) بنسخ منه متفقة. وقد تحصل له الثقة من نسخة غير موثوق بها في بعض المسائل إذا رأى الكلام منتظماً ، وهو خبير فطن لا يخفى عليه لدربته موضع (١) قوله: "مذهب ذلك الإمام " قال الملا على القاري في الموضوعات الكبرى". " ومن القواعد الكلية : أن نقل الأحاديث النبوية، والمسائل الفقهية، والتفاسير القرآنية، لا يجوز إلا من الكتب المتداولة ؛ لعدم الاعتماد على غيرها من وضع الزنادقة، وإلحاق الملاحدة، بخلاف الكتب المحفوظة ؛ فإن نسخها تكون صحيحة متعددة . (ص: ٤١٠) (٢) قوله : " وقد تحصل له الثقة" قال الإمام القرافي المالكي: "كان الأصل يقتضى أن لا تجوز الفتيا إلا بما يرويه العدل عن العدل عن المجتهد الذي يقلده المفتي، حتى يصح ذلك عند المفتى، كما تصح الأحاديث عند المجتهد ؛ لأنه نقل لدين الله تعالى في الموضعين، وعلى هذا كان ينبغي أن يحرم، غير أن الناس توسعوا في هذا العصر، فصاروا يفتون من كتب يطالعونها من غير رواية، وهو خطر عظيم في الدين، وخروج عن القواعد. غير أن الكتب المشهورة لشهرتها بعدت بعداً شديداً عن التحريف والتزوير، فاعتمد الناس عليها اعتمادًا على ظاهر الحال . وعلى هذا تحرم الفتوى من الكتب الغريبة التي لم تشتهر ، حتى تتظافر عليها الخواطر، ويعلم صحة ما فيها، وكذلك الكتب الحديثة التصنيف إذا لم يشتهر عزو ما فيها من النقول إلى الكتب المشهورة، أو يعلم أن مصنفها كان يعتمد هذا النوع من الصحة وهو موثوق بعدالته، وكذلك حواشى الكتب تحرم الفتوى بها ؛ لعدم صحتها والوثوق بها " . (الإحكام : ص ٣٦١) قيل : مراد الإمام القرافي إذا كانت الحواشى غريبة النقل، وأما إذا كان ما فيها موجوداً في الأمهات أو منسوباً إلى محله ، وهو بخط من يوثق به، فلا فرق بينها وبين سائر التصانيف، ولم تزل العلماء ينقلون ما على حواشى كتب الأئمة الموثوقة بعلمهم المعروفة خطوطهم، وإذا وجدوا حاشية يعرفون كاتبها نقلوا ذلك عنه، ونسبوها إليه، وأدخلوا ذلك في مصنفاتهم، وأما حيث يجهل الكاتب ويكون النقل غريباً فلا شك فيما قاله القرافي رحمه الله تعالى .

٦٤ - فإن لم يجده إلا في نسخة غير موثوق بها، فقال أبو عمرو : ينظر ، فإن وجده موافقا لأصول المذهب، وهو أهل لتخريج مثله في المذهب لو لم يجده منقولا ، فله أن يفتي به. فإن أراد حكايته عن قائله فلا يقل : "قال الشافعي -مثلا- كذا ، وليقل: "وجدت عن الشافعي كذا، أو بلغني عنه " ونحو هذا .
وإن لم يكن أهلا لتخريج مثله لم يجز له ذلك؛ فإن سبيله النقل المحض، ولم يحصل ما يجوز له ذلك (١) . وله أن يذكره لا على سبيل (١) قوله: "ما يجوز له ذلك هو الاعتماد على نسخة موثوق بها. هذا وقال العلامة ابن عابدین رحمه الله تعالى : " وطريق نقله لذلك إلى المجتهد أحد أمرين : إما أن يكون له سند فيه، أو يأخذه من كتاب معروف تداولته الأيدى نحو كتب محمد ابن الحسن، ونحوها من التصانيف المشهورة للمجتهدين؛ لأنه بمنزلة الخبر المتواتر المشهور، هكذا ذكر الرازي، فعلى هذا لو وجد بعض نسخ النوادر في زماننا، لا يحل عزو ما فيها إلى محمد ولا إلى أبي يوسف ؛ لأنها لم تشتهر في عصرنا في ديارنا ولم تتداول ، نعم إذا وجد النقل عن النوادر مثلا في کتاب مشهور معروف كالهداية والمبسوط، كان ذلك تعويلا على ذلك الكتاب، فتح، وأقره في البحر والنهر والمنح .
قلت : يلزم على هذا أن لا يجوز الآن النقل من أكثر الكتب المطولة من الشروح أو الفتاوى المشهورة أسماؤها لكنها لم تتداولها الأيدى حتى صارت بمنزلة الخير المتواتر المشهور ؛ لكونها لا توجد إلا في بعض المدارس أو عند بعض الناس كالمبسوط والمحيط والبدائع، وفيه نظر، بل الظاهر أنه لا يلزم التواتر بل يكفي غلبة الظن بكون ذلك الكتاب هو المسمى بذلك الاسم بأن وجد العلماء ينقلون عنه، ورأى ما نقلوه عنه موجوداً فيه أو وجد منه أكثر من نسخة ؛ فإنه يغلب على الظن أنه هو . ويدل على ذلك قوله : "إما أن يكون له سند فيه " أى فيما ينقله، والسند لا يلزم تواتره ولا شهرته وأيضا قدمنا أن القاضي إذا أشكل عليه أمر يكتب فيه إلى فقهاء مصر آخر، وأن المشاورة بالكتاب سنة قديمة فى الحوادث الشرعية، ولا شك أن احتمال التزوير فى هذا الكتاب اليسير أكثر من احتماله في شرح كبير بخط قديم، ولا سيما
Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi: He [the mufti] should only rely on a book whose authenticity is trusted, and that it represents the madhhab of that Imam (1). If he trusts that the original work is of this description, but this copy is not reliable, then he should verify with (2) agreeing copies of it. And he may gain confidence from an unreliable copy in some issues if he sees the text is well-arranged, and he is an expert and insightful, due to his experience, the place of (1) his statement: 'the madhhab of that Imam.' Al-Mulla 'Ali al-Qari said in al-Mawdu'at al-Kubra: 'Among the universal principles: that transmitting prophetic hadiths, fiqh issues, and Qur'anic tafsirs is not permissible except from well-known books; because there is no reliance on others due to the possibility of being fabricated by heretics or inserted by atheists, unlike preserved books, for their copies are authentic and numerous.' (p. 410) (2) His statement: 'he may gain confidence.' Imam al-Qarafi al-Maliki said: 'The original principle required that fatwa is not permissible except by narrations from reliable narrators to reliable narrators from the mujtahid whom the mufti follows, so that it is established for the mufti as hadiths are established for the mujtahid; because it is transmission of the religion of Allah in both places. On this basis, it should be prohibited, but people have become lenient in this era, so they give fatwa from books they read without [formal] narration, and this is a great danger in religion and departure from the principles. However, well-known books, due to their fame, have become greatly distant from distortion and forgery, so people rely on them based on apparent circumstances. On this basis, fatwa from obscure books that are not well-known is prohibited, until multiple minds concur on them and the correctness of their contents is known. Likewise, books recently authored, if the ascription of what they contain to well-known books is not known, or if it is not known that their author relied on this type of authenticity while being trustworthy in his integrity. Similarly, glosses on books (hawashi) are prohibited for fatwa due to lack of authenticity and trustworthiness.' (al-Ihkam: p. 361) It is said: Imam al-Qarafi intended when the glosses are strange in transmission. But if what they contain is present in the primary books or ascribed to its source, and it is in the handwriting of a trustworthy person, then there is no difference between them and other compositions. Scholars have always transmitted from the glosses of the books of trustworthy imams whose handwriting is known. And when they find a gloss whose author they know, they transmit from him and attribute it to him and include it in their works. But where the writer is unknown and the transmission is strange, there is no doubt about what al-Qarafi, may Allah have mercy on him, said. Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi: Deletion and Change. 51 64 - If he does not find it except in an unreliable copy, Abu 'Amr said: He should consider: if he finds it agreeing with the principles of the madhhab, and he is competent to derive similar rulings in the madhhab even if he had not found it transmitted, then he may give fatwa based on it. If he intends to relate it from its originator, he should not say: 'al-Shafi'i said such and such', but rather say: 'I found from al-Shafi'i such and such', or 'it reached me from him', and similar. And if he is not competent to derive similar rulings, it is not permissible for him to do so, because his way is pure transmission, and he has not attained what permits him to do that (1). And he may mention it not as a ... (1) His statement: 'what permits him to do that is reliance on a trustworthy copy.' And 'Allama Ibn 'Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'The path of his transmission of that to the mujtahid is one of two matters: either he has an isnad in it, or he takes it from a well-known book that has circulated among hands, such as the books of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and similar famous works of the mujtahids; because it is like mutawatir and well-known khabar. Thus mentioned al-Razi. On this basis, if one finds some copies of al-Nawadir in our time, it is not permissible to attribute what is in them to Muhammad or to Abu Yusuf, because they did not become famous in our time in our lands and did not circulate. Yes, if one finds a transmission from al-Nawadir, for example, in a famous and well-known book like al-Hidayah or al-Mabsut, then that is reliance on that book. Al-Fath, and it was confirmed in al-Bahr, al-Nahr, and al-Munyah. I say: It follows from this that now it is not permissible to transmit from most lengthy books of commentaries, or fatwa collections whose names are famous but have not circulated among hands such that they become like mutawatir and well-known khabar, because they are only found in some seminaries or with some people, like al-Mabsut, al-Muhit, and al-Bada'i. And there is consideration in this; rather it is apparent that tawatur is not necessary, rather a high probability (ghalabat al-zann) is sufficient that that book is the one called by that name, such that one finds scholars transmitting from it, and he sees what they transmitted from it present in it, or he finds more than one copy of it; for then it becomes highly probable that it is that book. And evidence for this is his statement: 'either he has an isnad in it' i.e., in what he transmits, and isnad does not require tawatur or fame. Also, we have previously stated that if a judge finds a matter difficult, he writes to the fuqaha of another Egypt, and that consultation by writing is an old sunna in legal incidents. And there is no doubt that the possibility of forgery in this small book is greater than its possibility in a large old commentary, especially ...
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage from Imam al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa, as commented upon by the author, establishes a critical rasm al-mufti rule: the mufti must only rely on books whose authenticity and representation of the madhhab are trustworthy. The commentary expands with two important fatwas. First, from Mulla 'Ali al-Qari, a universal principle: transmission of hadith, fiqh, and tafsir is not permissible except from well-known (mutadawala) books, because others may be corrupted by heretics. Only preserved books with multiple authentic copies are relied upon. Second, from Imam al-Qarafi, the original principle required formal narration (riwaya) from reliable transmitters, but due to later leniency, well-known books are accepted based on their fame shielding them from distortion. Fatwa from obscure books, newly authored books without known ascription to primary sources, and glosses (hawashi) is prohibited unless the gloss’s content is found in primary sources or written by a trustworthy person in known handwriting. The passage then presents Abu 'Amr's ruling: if a ruling is found only in an unreliable copy, the qualified mufti may still use it if it aligns with the principles of the madhhab and he is capable of deriving similar rulings. Otherwise, pure transmission is not allowed. The mufti must express caution by saying 'I found from al-Shafi'i' rather than 'al-Shafi'i said'. Ibn 'Abidin adds that transmission to the mujtahid requires either a valid isnad or reliance on a well-known book that has circulated like the works of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. Rare copies like al-Nawadir that are not famous in a region cannot be attributed directly to their authors. However, if the ruling is quoted in a famous book like al-Hidayah, that suffices. The commentator then argues that strict tawatur is not necessary; a high probability (ghalabat al-zann) from scholars transmitting from it, multiple copies, or internal consistency is sufficient. This is supported by the practice of judges writing to faraway fuqaha, where the small book may be more prone to forgery than a large old commentary. The passage thus provides a nuanced hierarchy of authoritative sources for the mufti.

Key Terms
كتاب موثوق بصحته (kitāb mawthūq bi-ṣiḥḥatihi): A book whose textual authenticity and attribution to the correct madhhab are established through fame (shuhra) or multiple copies.
نسخة غير موثوق بها (nuskhah ghayr mawthūq bihā): A copy of a book that is not reliably transmitted, possibly containing errors or alterations.
كتب متداولة (kutub mutadāwalah): Books that have been widely circulated and are well-known among scholars, considered safe from major tampering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a mufti do if he finds a ruling only in an unreliable copy?
A) He must discard it and not use it.
B) He may use it if it agrees with the principles of the madhhab and he can derive similar rulings.
C) He may only use it if he has a direct oral isnad from the imam.
D) He should attribute the ruling to the author by saying 'al-Shafi'i said'.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must verify the authority of his sources, but the Hanafi school grants flexibility to qualified scholars for reliable yet non-circulated texts.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

The Mufti's Duty: Verifying Multiple Reliable Sources
Ruling on mufti's reliance on few books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a Hanafi mufti must consult multiple authoritative books to identify the rajih opinion, and explain the consequences of relying on insufficient sources.

Core Idea
A mufti cannot be confident in one or two books; the rajih opinion must be verified across multiple authoritative transmissions.

Imam al-Nawawi's caution for Shafi'i muftis applies equally to Hanafi muftis: relying on a handful of books risks transmitting anomalous (shadh) opinions. The Hanafi mufti must consult the zahir al-riwayah texts and later authoritative works to determine the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the need for multiple sources
Recognize that legal rulings within a madhhab are transmitted through many books with varying degrees of reliability. A single source may contain a minority or anomalous view.
This is a foundational principle of rasm al-mufti.
2
Distinguish reliable from anomalous
Learn the Hanafi hierarchy of transmissions: Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core works of Muhammad al-Shaybani) are the most authoritative, followed by Nawadir, and then later fatwa collections. The mufti must know which sources carry weight.
Tarjih criteria include narrators' reliability and consistency with established usul.
3
Apply the rule to fatwa practice
When issuing a fatwa, do not rely on a single book. Cross-reference at least the six core works and later consolidations like Al-Hidayah, Al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and Radd al-Muhtar.
The mufta bihi opinion is the one supported by the majority of these sources.
4
Avoid common errors
Understand the danger of relying on a book that contains a shadh opinion not accepted by the majority. Verify the chain of transmission and the book's acceptance among the mutakhkhirin.
A book may be popular but carry weak opinions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦٥ قلت : لا يجوز لمفت على مذهب الشافعي إذا اعتمد النقل، أن يكتفى بمصنّف ومصنفين ونحوهما من كتب المتقدمين، وأكثر المتأخرين؛ لكثرة الاختلاف بينهم فى الجزم والترجيح ؛ لأن هذا المفتى المذكور إنما ينقل مذهب الشافعي ، ولا يحصل له وثوق بأن ما في المصنفين المذكورين ونحوهما هو مذهب الشافعي، أو الراجح منه ؛ لما فيها من الاختلاف. وهذا مما لا يتشكك فيه من له أدنى أنس بالمذهب، بل قد يجزم نحو عشرة من المصنفين بشيء وهو شاذ بالنسبة إلى الراجح في المذهب، ومخالف لما عليه الجمهور، وربما خالف نص الشافعي، أو نصوصاً له .
٦٦ - وسترى في هذا الشرح - إن شاء الله تعالى - أمثلة ذلك . وأرجو إن تم هذا الكتاب أنه يستغنى به عن كل ،مصنف، ويعلم به مذهب الشافعي علمًا قطعيًا إن شاء الله تعالى .
65 I say: It is not permissible for a mufti of the Shafi'i school, when relying on transmission, to be content with one or two works and the like from the books of the early scholars and most of the later ones, due to the abundance of disagreement among them in determination and preference. Because this mufti only transmits the Shafi'i school, and he does not gain confidence that what is in those two works and the like is the Shafi'i school, or the preferred opinion within it, because of the disagreement in them. This is something that anyone with the slightest familiarity with the school would not doubt. Rather, about ten authors may decisively state something that is anomalous relative to the preferred opinion in the school, contradicting the majority, and perhaps contradicting the explicit text of al-Shafi'i or multiple texts of his. 66 You will see examples of that in this commentary, Allah willing. I hope that if this book is completed, it will suffice for every other work, and one will learn the Shafi'i school with definitive knowledge, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the methodology of issuing fatwas within a madhhab. Imam al-Nawawi states that a mufti who follows the Shafi'i school must not be content with consulting only one or two books, whether early or later, because of the frequent disagreements within the school regarding which opinion is decisive or preferred. The mufti's role is to transmit the madhhab's position, not just any opinion found in a book. Many books contain views that are anomalous (shadh) and contradict the majority or even the explicit nass of al-Shafi'i. Without multiple reliable sources, the mufti cannot have confidence (wuthuq) that what he is transmitting is the correct position of the school. Al-Nawawi promises that his commentary will provide examples of this phenomenon and hopes it will become a definitive reference for the Shafi'i school. The rule is a direct admonition against lazy or superficial scholarship.

Key Terms
الراجح (al-rajih): The preferred or preponderant opinion within the madhhab, determined by the method of tarjih among conflicting transmissions.
النقل (al-naql): The transmission of the madhhab's rulings through authoritative books, as opposed to deriving directly from primary sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi application of this rasm al-mufti rule, which of the following is a valid practice for a mufti?
A) Rely on a single book if it is well-known and widely used.
B) Consult multiple books from the Zahir al-Riwayah and later authoritative works.
C) Only use the newest commentary because it supersedes all older works.
D) Ask another mufti instead of checking any books.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must cross-reference multiple authoritative transmissions to confidently transmit the rajih opinion of the madhhab.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Must a Mufti Renew Ijtihad for Recurring Cases?
Ruling on whether a mufti must re-examine when asked a similar case previously ruled

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on whether a mufti must renew his ijtihad when a similar case is presented again, and distinguish between the scenarios where the proof is remembered or not.

Core Idea
A mufti must renew his ijtihad for each new instance unless he remembers the ruling and its proof unchanged.

In the practice of ifta, a mufti often faces similar cases repeatedly. Should he simply repeat his previous fatwa or re-examine the issue? This passage from al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa presents the Shafi'i discussion, but the underlying principle is shared with the Hanafi school. The key is whether the mufti remembers both the ruling and its evidence, and whether circumstances have changed. This lesson will help you understand the conditions under which a mufti may rely on prior ijtihad and when fresh consideration is obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read paragraph 67. It distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) the mufti remembers both the fatwa and its proof, and (2) he remembers only the fatwa without the proof. Determine the ruling for each scenario according to the text.
The text says 'if he remembers... he may give a fatwa without renewed consideration' but if only the fatwa is remembered, the more correct view is wajib tajdid al-nazar.
2
Understand the exception for changed circumstances
Even in scenario (1), if the mufti suspects that his ijtihad might change upon re-examination, then renewing consideration is better. Identify the factor that triggers this exception.
The footnote says: 'unless he suspects by some indication that if he were to repeat the consideration, his ijtihad would change'.
3
Extend the rule to qadi and other practices
Paragraphs 68 and 69 analogize the mufti's situation to a qadi, and to practical matters like tayammum and qibla. Note how the same principle applies, and where there are two opinions (wajhan) in the Shafi'i school.
The extension shows the rule is not limited to fatwa but governs all ijtihad-based decisions.
4
Apply the Hanafi perspective
The Hanafi school modifies this rule based on the mufti's level. A mujtahid mufti may rely on his prior ijtihad unless new evidence arises; a muqallid mufti must consult the madhhab's authoritative texts and may not simply repeat his own fatwa. Evaluate the practical difference.
Refer to the madhhab dispute map in the toolbox.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثامنة :
٦٧ - إذا أفتى فى حادثة، ثم حدثت مثلها، فإن ذكر الفتوى الأولى ودليلها بالنسبة إلى أصل الشرع إن كان مستقلا، أو إلى مذهبه إن كان منتسبا ، أفتى بذلك بلا نظر (۱) . وإن ذكرها ولم يذكر دليلها، ولا طرأ ما يوجب رجوعه، فقيل له أن يفتى بذلك(1)، والأصح وجوب تجديد النظر (٢)
٦٨ - ومثله القاضى إذا حكم بالاجتهاد، ثم وقعت المسألة
٦٩ - وكذا تجديد الطلب في التيمم، والاجتهاد في القبلة وفيهما الوجهان (۳)
(۱) قوله : "أفتى بذلك بلا نظر " لعدم الحاجة إلى تجديد النظر ؛ لأنه تحصيل حاصل، ولأن الغرض من النظر أن تكون فتياه عن علم بما يفتى به، وذلك حاصل ، كما لو اجتهد في الحال، إلا أن يظن بأمارة أنه لو أعاد النظر تغير اجتهاده، فحينئذ إعادة النظر أولى .
(۲) قوله : والأصح وجوب تجديد النظر " لاحتمال تغير اجتهاده وظهور ما كان خافيا عنه ، وقيل : هذا إذا قامت لديه أمارة على وجود معارض لم يسبق له النظر فيه، أو أن اجتهاده قد يتغير لو أعاد النظر ؛ لتحصيله في الفترة علوماً مؤثرة في جهة النظر ، أو نحو ذلك، فإن ظهر ما يغير اجتهاده لم يجز له البقاء على القول الأول، ولا يجب عليه نقضه، ولا يكون اختلافه مع نفسه قادحًا في علمه، بل هذا من كمال عليه وورعه، ولأجل هذا خرج عن الأئمة في المسألة قولان فأكثر . راجع إعلام الموقعين : ٤ / ۲۳۲ ، والإحكام للآمدي : ٤٥٥،٤٥٤/٤ .
(۳) قوله : "وفيهما الوجهان" قال في "المهذب" في باب استقبال القبلة : " وإن صلى بالاجتهاد إلى جهة ثم حضرت صلاة أخرى ففيه وجهان أحدهما يصلى بالاجتهاد الأول ؛ لأنه قد عرف بالاجتهاد الأول والثاني : يلزمه أن يعيد الاجتهاد وهو منصوص في "الأم" ، كما تقول في الحاكم إذا اجتهد في حادثة ثم حدثت تلك الحادثة مرة أخرى " .
وفي شرحه للمصنف : الوجهان مشهوران أصحهما باتفاق الأصحاب : وجوب إعادة الاجتهاد وبه قطع كثيرون، وهو المنصوص في "الأم" ، وقد سبق مثلهما في المتيمم إذا طلب الماء فلم يجده وصلى وبقى في موضعه حتى حضرت صلاة أخرى قال الرافعي : قيل : الوجهان فيما إذا لم يفارق ،موضعه، فإن فارقه وجب الاجتهاد وجها واحداً كالتيمم، قال: ولكن الفرق ظاهر، ولا يحتاج إلى تجديد الاجتهاد للنافلة بلا خلاف" . المهذب على المجموع : ٢١٦/٣، ٢١٧)
The Eighth: 67 - If a mufti gave a fatwa on a case, then a similar case occurs, if he remembers the first fatwa and its proof relative to the source of the law if he is independent, or to his madhhab if he is affiliated, he may give a fatwa with it without renewed consideration (1). But if he remembers it without its proof, and nothing occurs to necessitate his retraction, then it is said he may give a fatwa with it (1), but the more correct view is the obligation of renewing consideration (2). 68 - And similarly, the qadi who ruled by ijtihad, then the same case occurs again. 69 - And likewise, the renewal of search in tayammum, and ijtihad regarding the qibla; and concerning these two, there are two opinions (3). (1) His saying: "he may give a fatwa with it without consideration" means there is no need to renew consideration because it is a redundant act, and because the purpose of consideration is that his fatwa be based on knowledge of what he is giving a fatwa on, and that is already attained, just as if he had made ijtihad presently, unless he suspects by some indication that if he were to repeat the consideration, his ijtihad would change; then repeating consideration is better. (2) His saying: "the more correct view is the obligation of renewing consideration" because of the possibility that his ijtihad may have changed and what was hidden from him became apparent. And it is said: this is if there arises for him an indication of the existence of an opposing factor not previously considered, or that his ijtihad might change if he repeats consideration due to his acquisition in the interim of knowledge influencing the direction of consideration, or something similar. If something appears that changes his ijtihad, he may not remain on the first opinion, nor is he obliged to overturn it. And his differing from his own earlier position does not impugn his knowledge; rather this is from his perfection and piety. For this reason, the imams have two or more opinions on the matter. (3) His saying: "and concerning these two, there are two opinions" — He said in al-Muhadhdhab in the chapter on facing the qibla: "If one prays by ijtihad facing a direction, then another prayer occurs, there are two opinions: one, he prays with the first ijtihad because he already knew by the first ijtihad; the second, he must repeat the ijtihad — and this is the explicit text in al-Umm, just as you say about the qadi who made ijtihad on a case and then that case occurs again." And in its commentary on the matn: "The two opinions are well-known; the more correct one by agreement of the companions is the obligation to repeat the ijtihad, and many decisively held this, and it is the explicit text in al-Umm. And the like of these two opinions has preceded regarding the person who performs tayammum when he searches for water and does not find it, then prays and remains in his place until another prayer occurs. Al-Rafi'i said: It is said that the two opinions apply when he has not left his place; if he left, ijtihad is obligatory as one view, like tayammum. He said: But the difference is apparent, and there is no need to renew ijtihad for a supererogatory prayer without disagreement." Al-Muhadhdhab with al-Majmu': 3/216-217.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage from al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa deals with a key methodological issue for muftis and judges: whether prior ijtihad suffices for a new similar case. It is presented as the eighth point (al-thamina). The ruling has two aspects: if the mufti remembers both the fatwa and its proof, he may rely on it without re-examination, because the effort (nazar) would be redundant (tahsil hasil). However, if he remembers only the ruling without the proof, there are two opinions. The more correct view (al-ashahh) is that he must renew his ijtihad, because his ijtihad may have changed or new evidence may have emerged. The same rule applies to a qadi who judges by ijtihad. The passage also extends to practical issues like tayammum and qibla direction, where there are two opinions in the Shafi'i school about repeating the search or ijtihad. The commentary in the footnotes explains the reasoning: the possibility of changed circumstances or new knowledge, and stresses that changing one's opinion does not impugn one's knowledge but shows piety. The Hanafi school similarly emphasizes the need for fresh consideration if the mufti's previous ruling was given without clear dalil or if circumstances change.

Key Terms
تجديد النظر (tajdid al-nazar): Renewing the intellectual consideration (ijtihad) for a case, rather than relying on a previous opinion.
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): The mental effort to derive a ruling from primary sources or to determine the preponderant opinion in a madhhab.
الوجهان (al-wajhan): Two opinions (wajh) within the Shafi'i school on a particular branch issue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the more correct view (al-ashahh) when a mufti is asked a similar case again and does not remember the proof of his first fatwa?
A) He must give fatwa based on the first fatwa
B) He must renew his ijtihad (tajdid al-nazar)
C) He must refuse to give a fatwa
D) He must seek a second opinion

Key Takeaway
A mufti must renew his ijtihad (tajdid al-nazar) for a recurring case unless he remembers both the ruling and its proof from a valid authority, with no suspicion of changed circumstances.
